<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2011 Super Outbreak</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Super_Outbreak_(disambiguation)" title="Super Outbreak (disambiguation)">Super Outbreak</a>.</div>

<sup>2</sup><small>Time from first tornado to last tornado</small></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2011 Super Outbreak</b> was the largest, costliest, and one of the deadliest <a href="/wiki/Tornado_outbreak" title="Tornado outbreak">tornado outbreaks</a> ever recorded, affecting the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midwest" title="Midwest">Midwestern</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeastern</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and leaving catastrophic destruction in its wake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaanews_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-noaanews-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The event affected <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a> the most severely, but it also produced destructive <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, and affected many other areas throughout the Southern and Eastern United States. In total, 362 tornadoes were confirmed by <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">NOAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> (NWS) and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">Government of Canada</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environment_Canada" title="Environment Canada">Environment Canada</a> in 21 states from <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State" title="New York State">New York</a> to southern <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. Widespread and destructive tornadoes occurred on each day of the outbreak, with April 27 being the most active day with a record of 218 tornadoes touching down that day from midnight to midnight <a href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone" title="Central Time Zone">CDT</a> (0500 – 0500 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>). Four of the tornadoes were destructive enough to be rated EF5, which is the highest ranking possible on the <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Fujita_scale" title="Enhanced Fujita scale">Enhanced Fujita scale</a>; typically these tornadoes are only recorded about once each year or less.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaanews_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-noaanews-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In total, 348 people were killed as a result of the outbreak, which includes 324 tornado-related deaths across six states and an additional 24 fatalities caused by other <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorm</a>-related events such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downbursts" title="Downbursts">straight-line winds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flash_flooding" title="Flash flooding">flash flooding</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alemapressrelease1_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-alemapressrelease1-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tuscaloosa_missing_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-tuscaloosa_missing-11">[11]</a></sup> In Alabama alone, 238 tornado-related deaths were confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/Storm_Prediction_Center" title="Storm Prediction Center">Storm Prediction Center</a> (SPC) and the state's <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management" title="Emergency management">Emergency Management Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc_fatal_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-spc_fatal-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alemapressrelease1_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-alemapressrelease1-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>April 27's 317 fatalities were the most tornado-related fatalities in the United States in a single day since the "<a href="/wiki/Tri-State_Tornado" title="Tri-State Tornado">Tri-State</a>" outbreak on March 18, 1925 (when at least 747 people were killed).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn1925outbreak_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn1925outbreak-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbsSouth_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbsSouth-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-second_deadliest_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-second_deadliest-15">[15]</a></sup> Nearly 500 preliminary <a href="/wiki/Local_storm_report" title="Local storm report">local storm reports</a> were received for tornadoes over four days, including 292 in 16 states on April 27 alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Reports_April_27_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Reports_April_27-16">[16]</a></sup> This event was the costliest tornado outbreak and one of the costliest natural disasters in United States history (even after adjustments for <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>), with total damages of approximately $11 billion (2011 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InsuranceNewsnet_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-InsuranceNewsnet-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_synopsis">Meteorological synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv/854px--Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:854px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="19.686333333333" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/7d/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv.480p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="505104" data-framerate="29.97002997003"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/7d/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv.360p.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&amp;quot;theora, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Ogg video (360P)" data-shorttitle="Ogg 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.ogv" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="589816" data-framerate="29.97002997003"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;'><img alt="File:Severe Tornado Outbreak in the Southern United States.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv/220px--Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv.jpg" style="width:220px;height:124px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Severe_Tornado_Outbreak_in_the_Southern_United_States.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This animation of satellite images from April 26 through the morning of April 28 shows the development of the weather system which spawned the tornadoes.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The outbreak was caused by a vigorous upper-level <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a> that moved into the Southern Plains states on April 25. An <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> developed ahead of this upper-level trough between northeastern <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> and western <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, which moved northeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SS11_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-SS11-17">[17]</a></sup> Conditions were similar on April 26, with a predicted likelihood of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severe_thunderstorm" title="Severe thunderstorm">severe thunderstorms</a>, including an extended threat of strong to violent long-track tornadoes during the afternoon and evening hours; mixed-layer <a href="/wiki/Convective_available_potential_energy" title="Convective available potential energy">CAPE</a> values were forecast to be around 3000–4000 J/kg, around east <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. The storm mode on April 26 was predicted to consist of mostly discrete <a href="/wiki/Supercell" title="Supercell">supercells</a> during the afternoon and early evening, shifting over to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoscale_Convective_Complex" title="Mesoscale Convective Complex">mesoscale convective complex</a>, with more of a threat of damaging winds and hail during the nighttime hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the storm system moved eastward toward the Ohio, Mississippi and Tennessee Valleys on April 27, a very powerful 80–100 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knot</a> mid-level <a href="/wiki/Jet_stream" title="Jet stream">jet stream</a> moved into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_Valley" title="Ohio Valley">Ohio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Valley" title="Tennessee Valley">Tennessee Valleys</a>, behind the trough, creating strong <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, with a low pressure center moving quickly northeastward across those areas on the 27th. On the afternoon of April 27, CAPE values were estimated to be in the range of 2000–3000 J/kg across Louisiana and southern Mississippi, with the moderate instability moving northeastward across the southern Tennessee Valley; in addition, temperatures across the southeastern United States ranged from the 70s°F (mid-20s°C) to the lower 90s°F (near 35 °C). <a href="/wiki/Hydrodynamical_helicity" title="Hydrodynamical helicity">Helicity</a> levels ranged from 450–600 m<sup>2</sup>/s<sup>2</sup>, which were supportive for significant tornadic activity and strong to violent long-track tornadoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In total, 56 severe weather watches (2011 watches, 199–256; two watches were omitted in error) were issued by the <a href="/wiki/Storm_Prediction_Center" title="Storm Prediction Center">Storm Prediction Center</a> (SPC) over those four days in the outbreak area, including 41 <a href="/wiki/Tornado_watch" title="Tornado watch">tornado watches</a> (10 of which were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particularly_dangerous_situation" title="Particularly dangerous situation">PDS watches</a>) and 15 <a href="/wiki/Severe_thunderstorm_watch" title="Severe thunderstorm watch">severe thunderstorm watches</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_25">April 25</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: April 25">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A large area of possible severe storms for April 25–27 was forecast as the <a href="/wiki/Storm_Prediction_Center" title="Storm Prediction Center">Storm Prediction Center</a> (SPC) issued a moderate risk of severe weather for three consecutive days, centered over Arkansas through Tennessee. At 3:25 p.m. <a href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone" title="Central Time Zone">CDT</a> (2025 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>), the SPC issued a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particularly_dangerous_situation" title="Particularly dangerous situation">Particularly dangerous situation</a> (PDS) <a href="/wiki/Tornado_watch" title="Tornado watch">tornado watch</a> for much of Arkansas and parts of Missouri, Oklahoma, Texas and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apr25SPC_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Apr25SPC-22">[22]</a></sup> By the evening hours of April 25, multiple tornadoes had been reported across a few states, including some that caused significant damage in <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>. An intense <a href="/wiki/Supercell" title="Supercell">supercell</a> thunderstorm tracked near the <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock,_Arkansas" title="Little Rock, Arkansas">Little Rock</a> metropolitan area and a <a href="/wiki/Tornado_emergency" title="Tornado emergency">tornado emergency</a> was declared for <a href="/wiki/Vilonia,_Arkansas" title="Vilonia, Arkansas">Vilonia, Arkansas</a>. A large <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Fujita_scale" title="Enhanced Fujita scale">EF2</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wedge_tornado" title="Wedge tornado">wedge</a> tornado struck the town, causing severe damage and killing four people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC_Arkansas_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC_Arkansas-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_York_Times_AR_Tornado_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_Times_AR_Tornado-24">[24]</a></sup> A strong EF3 tornado had also struck the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Springs_Village,_Arkansas" title="Hot Springs Village, Arkansas">Hot Springs Village</a> area earlier that evening, causing severe damage and one death. Another EF2 tornado caused extensive damage to a school building and <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock_Air_Force_Base" title="Little Rock Air Force Base">Little Rock Air Force Base</a> later that evening as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Severe <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flooding</a> continued across a large area from the <a href="/wiki/Red_River_of_the_South" title="Red River of the South">Red River</a> valley to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> A total of 42 tornadoes and four tornado-related deaths were confirmed on the 25th.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_26">April 26</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: April 26">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_SPC_high-risk_days" title="List of SPC high-risk days">high risk</a> of severe weather was issued for April 26 for portions of Louisiana, Arkansas, Oklahoma and Texas along and near the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_30" title="Interstate 30">Interstate 30</a> corridor as conditions became even more favorable for extreme weather.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HighRisk0426_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-HighRisk0426-27">[27]</a></sup> A large PDS tornado watch with very high tornado probabilities was issued that afternoon for that same area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Widespread <a href="/wiki/Tornado_warning" title="Tornado warning">tornado warnings</a> were issued in that area later that evening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tornado watches were also issued for the Lower Great Lakes in the afternoon hours, and supercells began to track across southern Michigan in the early evening. Two tornadoes touched down in Michigan and caused damage to farm structures. Further east, severe thunderstorms caused scattered wind damage and large hail across Pennsylvania and New York. Two-inch-diameter hail was reported in <a href="/wiki/Lock_Haven,_Pennsylvania" title="Lock Haven, Pennsylvania">Lock Haven, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Reports_April_26_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Reports_April_26-32">[32]</a></sup> An isolated supercell moved across Central New York throughout much of the afternoon, producing golf ball-sized hail in <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a>, and spawned a very brief EF1 tornado in <a href="/wiki/Verona_Mills,_New_York" title="Verona Mills, New York">Verona Mills</a>, causing primarily tree damage. Another tornado in <a href="/wiki/Gilbertsville,_New_York" title="Gilbertsville, New York">Gilbertsville</a> caused significant damage to an athletic field at a school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous tornadoes touched down across Texas, Louisiana, Arkansas, and several other states. Most of the tornadoes were weak, but a few caused considerable damage. A long-tracked wedge tornado caused EF2 damage along a path through rural portions of Texas and Louisiana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> An EF3 tornado destroyed multiple structures and caused severe damage at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Campbell,_Kentucky" title="Fort Campbell, Kentucky">Fort Campbell, Kentucky</a> as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> A total of 55 tornadoes were confirmed the 26th, though no fatalities occurred.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_27">April 27</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: April 27">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Doppler_Radar_Image_of_2011_Super_Outbreak.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="320" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Doppler_Radar_Image_of_2011_Super_Outbreak.png/220px-Doppler_Radar_Image_of_2011_Super_Outbreak.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6f/Doppler_Radar_Image_of_2011_Super_Outbreak.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Doppler_Radar_Image_of_2011_Super_Outbreak.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Doppler Radar Image taken of the Super Outbreak at 7:30am EST on April 27, 2011. Severe weather visible in Arkansas and Alabama.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Significant severe weather was ongoing at the start of April 27 and continued for the entire day virtually unbroken. For the second day in a row, the SPC issued a high risk of severe weather for the Southern United States, and late that morning the SPC increased the probability for tornadoes to 45 percent along a corridor from <a href="/wiki/Meridian,_Mississippi" title="Meridian, Mississippi">Meridian, Mississippi</a> to <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville, Alabama</a>, an extremely rare issuance exceeding the high risk standards. Conditions for tornadoes became increasingly favorable for an extreme tornado outbreak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Morning_squall_lines">Morning squall lines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Morning squall lines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the early morning hours, a cold front with several embedded low pressure areas extended from east <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> northeastward into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_River_Valley" title="Ohio River Valley">Ohio River Valley</a>. An upper-level disturbance that had moved across the frontal boundary the previous evening sparked an area of thunderstorms that morphed into a <a href="/wiki/Squall_line" title="Squall line">squall line</a>. This line of severe thunderstorms would be responsible for tornado actitvity from late on April 26 into the late morning of April 27. Early in the morning, the squall line, packing straight-line winds and numerous embedded tornadoes, moved through <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, then proceeded to affect <a href="/wiki/North_Alabama" title="North Alabama">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Alabama" title="Central Alabama">Central Alabama</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Tennessee" title="Middle Tennessee">Middle</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Tennessee" title="East Tennessee">East Tennessee</a>. The line strengthened as it moved through <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, due in part to a high amount of low-level moisture from the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> and increasing <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>.</p>
<p>Many of the tornadoes embedded in this initial squall line were weak, though several were strong and caused considerable damage. An EF3 caused major damage to homes in <a href="/wiki/Coaling,_Alabama" title="Coaling, Alabama">Coaling, Alabama</a>, an EF2 and an EF3 caused major damage and a fatality near <a href="/wiki/Eupora,_Mississippi" title="Eupora, Mississippi">Eupora, Mississippi</a>, and an EF3 caused heavy damage in downtown <a href="/wiki/Cordova,_Alabama" title="Cordova, Alabama">Cordova, Alabama</a>, which was struck by a deadly EF4 tornado later that afternoon. One embedded cell that began in <a href="/wiki/Cullman_County,_Alabama" title="Cullman County, Alabama">Cullman County, Alabama</a> produced a long-tracked EF2 that struck the town of <a href="/wiki/Hanceville,_Alabama" title="Hanceville, Alabama">Hanceville</a>, killing one person. That cell would go on to produce over ten tornadoes (mostly EF1s) to the northeast in <a href="/wiki/Marshall_County,_Alabama" title="Marshall County, Alabama">Marshall County</a> and another EF1 in <a href="/wiki/Dade_County,_Georgia" title="Dade County, Georgia">Dade County, Georgia</a>. The initial storms caused widespread <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_line" title="Power line">power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telephone_line" title="Telephone line">telephone line</a> outages across Alabama and Tennessee. This line of storms also caused some <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">NOAA</a> <a href="/wiki/NOAA_Weather_Radio" title="NOAA Weather Radio">weather radio</a> transmitter sites to stop functioning for the remainder of the outbreak. As a result, many people had no warning of approaching tornadoes later in the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27_Conditions_HUN_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-April_27_Conditions_HUN-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>From late morning to early afternoon, another squall line moved through northern parts of Mississippi and Alabama as high wind shear and low-level moisture persisted. However, this time several discrete <a href="/wiki/Supercell" title="Supercell">supercells</a> developed along and in front of the line, spawning seven weak tornadoes across <a href="/wiki/Morgan_County,_Alabama" title="Morgan County, Alabama">Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limestone_County,_Alabama" title="Limestone County, Alabama">Limestone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madison_County,_Alabama" title="Madison County, Alabama">Madison</a> Counties in northern Alabama around noon that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27_Conditions_HUN_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-April_27_Conditions_HUN-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Afternoon_supercells">Afternoon supercells</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Afternoon supercells">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia,_MS_ground_scouring.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="723" data-file-width="968" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Philadelphia%2C_MS_ground_scouring.jpg/220px-Philadelphia%2C_MS_ground_scouring.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Philadelphia%2C_MS_ground_scouring.jpg/330px-Philadelphia%2C_MS_ground_scouring.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Philadelphia%2C_MS_ground_scouring.jpg/440px-Philadelphia%2C_MS_ground_scouring.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Philadelphia,_MS_ground_scouring.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Extremely deep ground scouring near <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Mississippi" title="Philadelphia, Mississippi">Philadelphia, Mississippi</a> caused by a fast-moving EF5 tornado that killed three people.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most prolific supercells of the outbreak developed shortly after noon in Mississippi and began to track eastward. During the early afternoon, as wind shear and low-level moisture continued to increase dramatically, a <a href="/wiki/Tornado_emergency" title="Tornado emergency">tornado emergency</a> was declared for <a href="/wiki/Neshoba_County,_Mississippi" title="Neshoba County, Mississippi">Neshoba County, Mississippi</a> as a large tornado was reported on the ground by storm spotters and a camera atop a television tower from <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WTOK-TV" title="WTOK-TV">WTOK-TV</a> (channel 11) in <a href="/wiki/Meridian,_Mississippi" title="Meridian, Mississippi">Meridian, Mississippi</a>. This powerful EF5 tornado caused incredible damage northeast of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Mississippi" title="Philadelphia, Mississippi">Philadelphia, Mississippi</a>, where pavement was torn from roads, vehicles were thrown, and the ground was scoured out to a depth of 2 feet (0.61 m) by the tornado. Three people died in this tornado when a mobile home was picked up and thrown 300 yards (270 m) into a wooded area, being obliterated in the process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Another very long-tracked EF4 tornado passed near the town of <a href="/wiki/Enterprise,_Mississippi" title="Enterprise, Mississippi">Enterprise, Mississippi</a>, killing seven people before crossing into Alabama and eventually dissipating. In response to the high risk issued by the SPC and the already unstable atmosphere expected to become even more unstable through the afternoon hours, a <a href="/wiki/Particularly_Dangerous_Situation" title="Particularly Dangerous Situation">PDS</a> <a href="/wiki/Tornado_watch" title="Tornado watch">tornado watch</a> was issued at 1:45 p.m. CDT (1845 UTC) for much of Alabama and portions of Mississippi, Tennessee, and Georgia. A widespread complex of supercell storms overspread the states of Mississippi and Alabama and violent tornadoes began rapidly touching down as the evening progressed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27_Conditions_HUN_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-April_27_Conditions_HUN-37">[37]</a></sup> Four tornadoes were officially rated as EF5 on the <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Fujita_scale" title="Enhanced Fujita scale">Enhanced Fujita scale</a> that day. One of these EF5s obliterated the town of <a href="/wiki/Smithville,_Mississippi" title="Smithville, Mississippi">Smithville, Mississippi</a>, where many well-built brick homes were reduced to bare slabs, numerous hardwood trees were completely debarked, and an SUV was hurled half a mile into the top of the town's water tower, leaving a visible dent. Another long-tracked EF5 wedge tornado passed through rural portions of Alabama and Tennessee, becoming the deadliest tornado of the outbreak as it completely devastated the towns of <a href="/wiki/Hackleburg,_Alabama" title="Hackleburg, Alabama">Hackleburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Campbell,_Alabama" title="Phil Campbell, Alabama">Phil Campbell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Hope,_Lawrence_County,_Alabama" title="Mount Hope, Lawrence County, Alabama">Mount Hope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanner,_Alabama" title="Tanner, Alabama">Tanner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harvest,_Alabama" title="Harvest, Alabama">Harvest</a>, killing 72 people. This marks only the second day in history (the other being the April 3, 1974 <a href="/wiki/1974_Super_Outbreak" title="1974 Super Outbreak">Super Outbreak</a>) that there were more than two F5/EF5 tornadoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornadoes continued to track through central Alabama that afternoon and into the early evening hours. A dangerous and destructive tornado struck the city of <a href="/wiki/Cullman,_Alabama" title="Cullman, Alabama">Cullman, Alabama</a> at around 3:00 p.m. CDT (2000 UTC). This large, multiple-vortex tornado was captured on several tower cameras from <a href="/wiki/Television_station" title="Television station">television stations</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WBRC" title="WBRC">WBRC</a> (channel 6) and ABC affiliate <a href="/wiki/WBMA-LD" title="WBMA-LD">WBMA-LD</a>/<a href="/wiki/WSES" title="WSES">WCFT-TV</a>/<a href="/wiki/WGWW" title="WGWW">WJSU-TV</a> (channels 58, 33, and 40) out of <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham</a>. The tornado caused extensive destruction in downtown Cullman, a city of about 20,000 people; the tornado was ultimately rated an EF4. The final damage count was 867 residences and 94 businesses in Cullman, and 6 people were killed throughout the path.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The town of <a href="/wiki/Cordova,_Alabama" title="Cordova, Alabama">Cordova, Alabama</a>, which had already been damaged by an EF3 tornado from the initial round of storms, was struck by an EF4 tornado that killed 13 people. Two violent EF4 tornadoes also ripped through <a href="/wiki/Jackson_County,_Alabama" title="Jackson County, Alabama">Jackson County, Alabama</a>, one of which caused a fatality near <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_Alabama" title="Bridgeport, Alabama">Bridgeport</a>, while the other passed near <a href="/wiki/Pisgah,_Alabama" title="Pisgah, Alabama">Pisgah</a> and into Georgia where it caused major damage in <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_Georgia" title="Trenton, Georgia">Trenton</a>, killing 14 people along its path. At around 5:10 p.m. CDT (2210 UTC), a very large and exceptionally destructive tornado struck <a href="/wiki/Tuscaloosa,_Alabama" title="Tuscaloosa, Alabama">Tuscaloosa, Alabama</a>, and about 40 minutes later, the same tornado struck the northern suburbs of nearby Birmingham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massive_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-massive-41">[41]</a></sup> A tornado emergency was issued for both cities, along with many other cities that day. Many local television stations, including WBRC and WBMA-LD/WCFT/WJSU, as well as <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WIAT" title="WIAT">WIAT</a> (channel 42), broadcast live footage of this long-tracked tornado in both Tuscaloosa and Birmingham. A debris ball was observed by the Birmingham <a href="/wiki/NEXRAD" title="NEXRAD">NEXRAD</a>, indicating that the tornado was causing extreme damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> This tornado killed 64 people and caused extensive devastation in densely populated areas, and the tornado struck several of the same small communities as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_1956_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1956 Birmingham tornado">April 1956 F4</a>, the <a href="/wiki/April_1977_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1977 Birmingham tornado">April 1977 F5</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_1998_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1998 Birmingham tornado">April 1998 F5 tornadoes</a> that hit portions of the Birmingham area. The supercell responsible for the Tuscaloosa/Birmingham EF4 tornado originated in <a href="/wiki/Newton_County,_Mississippi" title="Newton County, Mississippi">Newton County, Mississippi</a>. The supercell also produced an EF4 tornado later that evening that killed 22 people as it struck areas in and around <a href="/wiki/Ohatchee,_Alabama" title="Ohatchee, Alabama">Ohatchee, Alabama</a> before eventually crossing into Georgia and causing additional damage near <a href="/wiki/Cave_Spring,_Georgia" title="Cave Spring, Georgia">Cave Spring</a> before dissipating. Further to the south, a mile-wide EF3 tornado killed 7 people in mostly rural areas and caused major damage in the small town of <a href="/wiki/Eoline,_Alabama" title="Eoline, Alabama">Eoline</a>. The final EF5 tornado of the day caused remarkable damage in and around the town of <a href="/wiki/Rainsville,_Alabama" title="Rainsville, Alabama">Rainsville, Alabama</a>, killing 25 people before crossing into Georgia and dissipating. Tornadoes continued to touch down further to the northeast as the sun set, particularly in Georgia. This included a long-tracked EF4 that caused major damage in <a href="/wiki/Ringgold,_Georgia" title="Ringgold, Georgia">Ringgold, Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apison,_Tennessee" title="Apison, Tennessee">Apison, Tennessee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Tennessee" title="Cleveland, Tennessee">Cleveland, Tennessee</a>, killing 20 people along the path. After dark, violent tornadoes continued to touch down, and a nighttime EF4 tornado destroyed many lakeside homes at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Martin" title="Lake Martin">Lake Martin</a> in eastern Alabama, killing 7 people. Additional strong nighttime tornadoes occurred in Georgia, including an EF3 that killed two people in <a href="/wiki/Barnesville,_Georgia" title="Barnesville, Georgia">Barnesville</a>, and another EF3 that destroyed multiple homes and killed one person at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Burton_(Georgia)" title="Lake Burton (Georgia)">Lake Burton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_activity_farther_east">Continued activity farther east</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Continued activity farther east">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Powerful tornadoes touched down across <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> as well that evening. A violent EF4 struck the community of <a href="/wiki/New_Harmony,_Tennessee" title="New Harmony, Tennessee">New Harmony, Tennessee</a>, where homes were leveled, vehicles were tossed, and four people were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Two EF3 tornadoes crossed paths in <a href="/wiki/Greene_County,_Tennessee" title="Greene County, Tennessee">Greene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_County,_Tennessee" title="Washington County, Tennessee">Washington</a> counties (coming a couple hours apart), resulting in 8 fatalities. The rural communities of <a href="/wiki/Horse_Creek,_Tennessee" title="Horse Creek, Tennessee">Horse Creek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camp_Creek,_Tennessee" title="Camp Creek, Tennessee">Camp Creek</a> suffered major damage from those tornadoes late that evening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> A very large EF4 wedge tornado leveled a mile-wide swath of forest though 14 miles (23 km) of <a href="/wiki/Great_Smoky_Mountains_National_Park" title="Great Smoky Mountains National Park">Great Smoky Mountains National Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Chilhowee_Dam" title="Chilhowee Dam">Chilhowee Lake</a>, large metal power line truss towers were torn and thrown from their concrete supports that they were anchored to.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>A secondary area of severe weather also developed that afternoon and evening along the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_81" title="Interstate 81">Interstate 81</a> corridor from central and northern <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> northward through <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, continuing into early April 28. Many tornadoes touched down in this area as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Most of these tornadoes were weak, though an EF2 tornado touched down near the town of <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Virginia" title="Halifax, Virginia">Halifax, Virginia</a>, and caused severe damage to homes in the area, resulting in one death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Tornado alerts were issued for <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern Ontario</a> as far north as <a href="/wiki/Ottawa" title="Ottawa">Ottawa</a> as well; one tornado was later confirmed in <a href="/wiki/Fergus,_Ontario" title="Fergus, Ontario">Fergus, Ontario</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:April_27,_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="721" data-file-width="1070" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/April_27%2C_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG/220px-April_27%2C_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/April_27%2C_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG/330px-April_27%2C_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/April_27%2C_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG/440px-April_27%2C_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:April_27,_2011_severe_weather_warnings.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of all tornado (red), severe thunderstorm (yellow), and flood (green) warnings issued on April 27.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A statewide review by emergency management officials recorded 249 fatalities in Alabama, 23 of which were not tornado-related.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alemapressrelease1_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-alemapressrelease1-10">[10]</a></sup> Damage and power outages in the <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville</a> area were so widespread that at one point over 650,000 people were out of power in the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Valley_Authority" title="Tennessee Valley Authority">Tennessee Valley Authority</a> system. The EF5 tornado that struck Hackleburg and Phil Campbell eventually damaged main power lines coming from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Browns_Ferry_Nuclear_Plant" title="Browns Ferry Nuclear Plant">Browns Ferry Nuclear Plant</a> further to the northeast. These towers were the main supply of electrical power to much of North Alabama and some were without power for two weeks. The tornado just missed the Limestone Correctional Facility, which less than a year later would be struck by another tornado.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Storm Prediction Center received 292 reports of tornadoes in the preceding 24 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Reports_April_27_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Reports_April_27-16">[16]</a></sup> It broke the record for the most tornado touchdowns in 24 hours with 219 in the United States from midnight to midnight CDT (0500 – 0500 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>) breaking the 24-hour record of 147 (in both totals, excluding confirmed tornadoes outside the United States that were part of the outbreak) set by the <a href="/wiki/1974_Super_Outbreak" title="1974 Super Outbreak">1974 Super Outbreak</a>. Of those 219 tornadoes, 59 touched down in Alabama and 79 hit the ground in Tennessee, accounting for well over half of the tornadoes that touched down on April 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> On April 27 alone, the National Weather Service in Huntsville, Alabama issued 92 tornado warnings, 31 <a href="/wiki/Severe_thunderstorm_warning" title="Severe thunderstorm warning">severe thunderstorm warnings</a>, and seven <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood_warning" title="Flash flood warning">flash flood warnings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWDJW-04272011-WarningSummaries_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-SWDJW-04272011-WarningSummaries-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_28">April 28</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: April 28">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tornado watches were issued for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> coast from <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> to <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> at the start of the day and continued through the morning and early afternoon, but tornadoes were forecasted to generally be weaker and more isolated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Despite this, the secondary portion of the outbreak that had begun producing scattered tornadoes throughout the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Mid-Atlantic</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a> regions the previous evening intensified during the early hours of the morning, producing numerous tornadoes in <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost1_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost1-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>. While most were weak, some of the tornadoes that struck portions of Virginia, New York, and Pennsylvania were strong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Although tornado watches were issued, no tornadoes were spotted in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost1_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost1-60">[60]</a></sup> In the wake of the tornadoes and severe thunderstorms, widespread flooding hit the Midwest, South, and Eastern Seaboard, with extensive flood and flash flood warnings issued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> One particularly damaging and deadly EF3 tornado struck the town of <a href="/wiki/Glade_Spring,_Virginia" title="Glade Spring, Virginia">Glade Spring, Virginia</a> very early in the morning, where three people died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The last tornadoes of the outbreak touched down that afternoon in eastern <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, which was hard hit in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_14%E2%80%9316,_2011_tornado_outbreak" title="April 14–16, 2011 tornado outbreak">April 16 outbreak</a>, though the tornadoes that impacted the area this time around were weak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The system moved out into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> that evening, with the exception of isolated thunderstorms over central Florida that night into April 29, although there were no tornadoes then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_tornadoes">Notable tornadoes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Notable tornadoes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vilonia.2C_Arkansas">Vilonia, Arkansas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Vilonia, Arkansas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vilonia2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Vilonia2011.jpg/255px-Vilonia2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Vilonia2011.jpg/383px-Vilonia2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Vilonia2011.jpg/510px-Vilonia2011.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vilonia2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Remains of a mobile home that was destroyed by the Vilonia tornado.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first tornado of the outbreak to cause multiple deaths was a long-tracked, high-end EF2 wedge tornado that struck the small town of <a href="/wiki/Vilonia,_Arkansas" title="Vilonia, Arkansas">Vilonia, Arkansas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Faulkner_County,_Arkansas" title="Faulkner County, Arkansas">Faulkner County</a> around 7:30 p.m. <a href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone" title="Central Time Zone">CDT</a> (0030 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>) on April 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSLittleRockApril27_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSLittleRockApril27-70">[70]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Tornado_warning" title="Tornado warning">tornado warning</a> was issued for the town roughly 30 minutes prior to the tornado's arrival, and the relatively low loss of life was attributed to this lead time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheCabin426_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheCabin426-71">[71]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Tornado_emergency" title="Tornado emergency">tornado emergency</a> was declared at 7:24 p.m. CDT (0024 UTC) for Vilonia shortly before the tornado struck.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Four people were killed in the town and many more were injured. The tornado touched down northwest of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ferndale,_Arkansas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ferndale, Arkansas (page does not exist)">Ferndale</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pulaski_County,_Arkansas" title="Pulaski County, Arkansas">Pulaski County</a> at 6:48 p.m. CDT (2348 UTC), downing trees and transmission towers at EF1 intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> It continued northeast of <a href="/wiki/Natural_Steps,_Arkansas" title="Natural Steps, Arkansas">Natural Steps</a>, severely damaging a small church and downing numerous trees, one of which landed on a house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The tornado continued to knock down trees as it passed near <a href="/wiki/Roland,_Arkansas" title="Roland, Arkansas">Roland</a>, several of which landed on homes. The tornado reached EF2 strength as it crossed into Faulkner County and passed southeast of <a href="/wiki/Mayflower,_Arkansas" title="Mayflower, Arkansas">Mayflower</a>, downing numerous trees and power lines and damaging homes and outbuildings. Past Mayflower, it continued towards Vilonia and struck a mobile home park, where numerous mobile homes were destroyed and the four fatalities occurred. Two of the fatalities occurred when a couple attempted to take shelter in a cargo container, which was thrown 150 yards (140 m) and deposited near a pond. Several other people were injured in this area as well. The tornado maintained EF2 intensity as it moved directly through Vilonia, damaging numerous homes and businesses and flipping several semi-trucks. The <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">American Red Cross</a> indicated that approximately 34 site-built houses and 62 mobile homes were destroyed, 91 site-built homes and 41 mobile homes suffered major damage, 145 site-built houses and 43 mobile homes had minor damage, and 53 site-built houses and 38 mobile homes were affected in some other way in the Vilonia area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> One of the mobile homes was picked up and flipped, and the home's two bathtubs were found over a hill about 40 yards (37 m) away. The lone occupant of the mobile home sustained major injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> After moving through Vilonia, the tornado weakened to EF1 strength as it moved into <a href="/wiki/White_County,_Arkansas" title="White County, Arkansas">White County</a> and passed west of <a href="/wiki/El_Paso,_Arkansas" title="El Paso, Arkansas">El Paso</a>, where trees were blown over onto houses (damaging several roofs), barns and outbuildings were destroyed, an <a href="/wiki/Recreational_vehicle" title="Recreational vehicle">RV</a> and the trailer portion of a tractor-trailer were overturned, and hundreds of trees were downed. The tornado finally dissipated north of <a href="/wiki/Joy,_Arkansas" title="Joy, Arkansas">Joy</a> at 7:59 p.m. CDT (0059 UTC), after having travelled just over 51 miles (82 km). At its widest point, the tornado was 1.64 miles (2.64 km) wide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheCabin426_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-TheCabin426-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Following the tornado, 85 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">U.S. National Guard</a> were deployed to assist in search and rescue, debris clearing, security and traffic control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 27, 2014, three years and two days after this tornado, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_27%E2%80%9330,_2014_tornado_outbreak" title="April 27–30, 2014 tornado outbreak">a violent EF4 tornado</a> touched down west of Ferndale and moved along almost the same path as this tornado, causing 16 fatalities and many injuries. However, it affected more of Mayflower than this tornado did and caused greater damage all along the path, especially in Vilonia, before lifting near El Paso.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSLittleRockApril27Vilonia_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSLittleRockApril27Vilonia-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philadelphia.E2.80.93Kemper_County.2C_Mississippi">Philadelphia–Kemper County, Mississippi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Philadelphia–Kemper County, Mississippi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Philadelphia,_Mississippi_tornado" title="2011 Philadelphia, Mississippi tornado">2011 Philadelphia, Mississippi tornado</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:April_27,_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="723" data-file-width="968" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/April_27%2C_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg/220px-April_27%2C_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/April_27%2C_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg/330px-April_27%2C_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/April_27%2C_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg/440px-April_27%2C_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:April_27,_2011_Mississippi_tornado_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A car that was thrown against a stand of trees by the Philadelphia tornado.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first EF5 tornado of the outbreak touched down in the city of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Mississippi" title="Philadelphia, Mississippi">Philadelphia, Mississippi</a> on April 27. The tornado hit the ground at 2:30 p.m. CDT (1930 UTC) and traveled for nearly 29 miles (47 km) through <a href="/wiki/Neshoba_County,_Mississippi" title="Neshoba County, Mississippi">Neshoba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kemper_County,_Mississippi" title="Kemper County, Mississippi">Kemper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winston_County,_Mississippi" title="Winston County, Mississippi">Winston</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Noxubee_County,_Mississippi" title="Noxubee County, Mississippi">Noxubee</a> counties, reaching a maximum width of a <span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span>-mile (0.80 km).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey-81">[81]</a></sup> The tornado killed three people, injured eight others, and caused $1.1 million in damage across its path.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The supercell thunderstorm that produced this tornado formed around 1:00 p.m. CDT south of Jackson, Mississippi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaEF5_1_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaEF5_1-83">[83]</a></sup> Traveling briskly to the northeast, it became severe within 25 minutes and potentially tornadic by 1:36 p.m. CDT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaEF5_1_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaEF5_1-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> A tornado finally touched down at 2:30 p.m. CDT just east of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Municipal_Airport" title="Philadelphia Municipal Airport">Philadelphia Municipal Airport</a>. It quickly intensified and began producing EF5 damage by 2:38 p.m. CDT; extreme ground scouring, up to 2 feet (0.61 m) deep in places, occurred in northeastern Neshoba County. After crossing into Kemper County, the tornado obliterated a mobile home, killing all three inside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey-81">[81]</a></sup> It reached EF5 strength a second time near the Kemper–Winston county line where extreme ground scouring again took place and pavement was scoured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhiladelphiaEF5_1_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-PhiladelphiaEF5_1-83">[83]</a></sup> Extreme tree damage took place along the track and it ultimately dissipated at 3:00 p.m. CDT about 6 miles (9.7 km) north of <a href="/wiki/Mashulaville,_Mississippi" title="Mashulaville, Mississippi">Mashulaville</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey_81-4"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>This was the first tornado to cause F5/EF5 damage in <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a> since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Candlestick_Park_tornado" title="Candlestick Park tornado">Candlestick Park tornado</a> of March 3, 1966. Additionally, the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Smithville,_Mississippi" title="Smithville, Mississippi">Smithville</a> tornado later that day marked the first time since statistics have been kept that two EF5 tornadoes have been recorded on the same day in Mississippi. Prior to this, the last confirmed EF5 tornado was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parkersburg_Tornado" title="Parkersburg Tornado">Parkersburg, Iowa tornado</a> of May 25, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey_81-5"><a href="#cite_note-Philadelphia.2C_MS_EF5_Survey-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cullman.2FArab.2C_Alabama">Cullman/Arab, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cullman/Arab, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="431" data-file-width="717" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg/255px-Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg/383px-Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg/510px-Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cullman_Alabama_First_Methodist_Church_Damage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Damage to the First Methodist Church in downtown <a href="/wiki/Cullman,_Alabama" title="Cullman, Alabama">Cullman, Alabama</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rated an EF4, this highly visible multiple-vortex tornado tracked directly through downtown Cullman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Long_Track_Tornado_Hits_Cullman.2C_Alabama_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Long_Track_Tornado_Hits_Cullman.2C_Alabama-85">[85]</a></sup> The tornado touched down at 2:40 p.m. CDT (1940 UTC) on April 27 and tracked a 47-mile (76 km) damage path through <a href="/wiki/Cullman_County,_Alabama" title="Cullman County, Alabama">Cullman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_County,_Alabama" title="Morgan County, Alabama">Morgan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_County,_Alabama" title="Marshall County, Alabama">Marshall</a> counties, resulting in six fatalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cullman tornado first touched down on the north side of <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Smith_Lake" title="Lewis Smith Lake">Lewis Smith Lake</a> and caused light structural damage near <a href="/wiki/Crane_Hill,_Alabama" title="Crane Hill, Alabama">Crane Hill</a> before intensifying and tracking directly towards Cullman, snapping numerous trees and heavily damaging several homes. The tornado became violent as it entered Cullman, being tracked and broadcast live via several tower cameras, including one operated by <a href="/wiki/WBMA-LD" title="WBMA-LD">ABC 33/40</a>, for several minutes. That camera captured the destruction of a communications tower belonging to Cullman area <a href="/wiki/Low-power_broadcasting" title="Low-power broadcasting">low-power</a> television station <a href="/wiki/WCQT-LP" title="WCQT-LP">WCQT-LP</a> as the tornado passed through the city. Radio stations in downtown Cullman also reported on the tornado and some even captured the tornado passing over until power was knocked out. The courthouse and nearby emergency management building took a direct hit from the tornado, both sustaining considerable damage, and two school buildings were heavily damaged as well. Many well-known businesses such as Vincent's Furniture, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cullman_Times" title="The Cullman Times">The Cullman Times</a></i>, and the Busy Bee Cafe were also either severely damaged or destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Long_Track_Tornado_Hits_Cullman.2C_Alabama_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-Long_Track_Tornado_Hits_Cullman.2C_Alabama-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cullman2011EF4.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="674" data-file-width="899" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cullman2011EF4.JPG/220px-Cullman2011EF4.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cullman2011EF4.JPG/330px-Cullman2011EF4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Cullman2011EF4.JPG/440px-Cullman2011EF4.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cullman2011EF4.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Major structural damage to businesses in downtown Cullman.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Downtown Cullman was badly damaged by the tornado, with the major damage being along a two-block area through the center of the downtown business district. The tornado more or less followed <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_278" title="U.S. Route 278">U.S. Highway 278</a> through the city, which in turn led to the tornado crossing and creating extensive damage along many major intersections, including those with <a href="/wiki/Interstate_65_in_Alabama" title="Interstate 65 in Alabama">Interstate 65</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_31_in_Alabama" title="U.S. Route 31 in Alabama">U.S. Highway 31</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_157" title="Alabama State Route 157">State Route 157</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_69" title="Alabama State Route 69">State Route 69</a>. Numerous well-built brick buildings and storefronts in downtown Cullman were heavily damaged or completely destroyed, along with multiple churches. Many homes were damaged or destroyed in residential areas of the city, with extensive tree and power line damage noted as well. In all, a total of 867 residences and 94 businesses within the city of Cullman were damaged or destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado continued northeast, becoming large and wedge-shaped. It then passed just north of <a href="/wiki/Fairview,_Alabama" title="Fairview, Alabama">Fairview</a>, completely destroying multiple homes and debarking numerous hardwood trees. Pieces of debris were found speared through vehicles in this area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado_86-2"><a href="#cite_note-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado-86">[86]</a></sup> The tornado then briefly passed through a section of <a href="/wiki/Morgan_County,_Alabama" title="Morgan County, Alabama">Morgan County</a> near the town of <a href="/wiki/Hulaco,_Alabama" title="Hulaco, Alabama">Hulaco</a>, destroying several older block-foundation homes and snapping numerous large trees off at the base. The tornado then crossed into <a href="/wiki/Marshall_County,_Alabama" title="Marshall County, Alabama">Marshall County</a> and impacted the rural community of <a href="/wiki/Ruth,_Alabama" title="Ruth, Alabama">Ruth</a>, just north of <a href="/wiki/Arab,_Alabama" title="Arab, Alabama">Arab</a>. A large but poorly-anchored brick home was swept completely away in this area, with the debris scattered 100 yards from the foundation. Several large trees on the property were ripped out of the ground and missing, along with a trailer that was unable to be located at the time of the survey. Multiple other homes and structures were impacted in the Ruth area, and a gas station was completely destroyed. A shed was destroyed with pieces of large farm machinery stored inside thrown up to 20 yards away, a storage trailer was tossed 100 yards and found impaled by multiple planks of wood, and concrete power poles in the area were bent over. Arab's power grid was completely crippled by the tornado's effects, and many roads in the area were obstructed by downed trees and power lines. The tornado damaged and destroyed several other homes, garages, and sheds north of <a href="/wiki/Union_Grove,_Alabama" title="Union Grove, Alabama">Union Grove</a> before it crossed the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_River" title="Tennessee River">Tennessee River</a>, snapping numerous trees in a forested area before dissipating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado_86-3"><a href="#cite_note-April_27.2C_2011_Cullman.2C_Alabama_EF4_Tornado-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hackleburg.E2.80.93Phil_Campbell.E2.80.93Tanner.E2.80.93Harvest.2C_Alabama.2FHuntland.2C_Tennessee">Hackleburg–Phil Campbell–Tanner–Harvest, Alabama/Huntland, Tennessee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hackleburg–Phil Campbell–Tanner–Harvest, Alabama/Huntland, Tennessee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Hackleburg%E2%80%93Phil_Campbell,_Alabama_tornado" title="2011 Hackleburg–Phil Campbell, Alabama tornado">2011 Hackleburg–Phil Campbell, Alabama tornado</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="900" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg/220px-Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg/330px-Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg/440px-Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phil_Campbell_tornado_damage2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
EF5 damage in Phil Campbell, with multiple homes swept away and grass scoured from hillsides.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This devastating, long-tracked, EF5 wedge tornado was the deadliest of the outbreak. It first touched down in <a href="/wiki/Marion_County,_Alabama" title="Marion County, Alabama">Marion County, Alabama</a> about 5 miles (8.0 km) west-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Alabama" title="Hamilton, Alabama">Hamilton</a> around 3:00 p.m. CDT (2100 UTC) on April 27, leaving massive damage along its track. The storm would eventually reach the <a href="/wiki/Hackleburg,_Alabama" title="Hackleburg, Alabama">Hackleburg</a> area, completely leveling many homes and businesses, including a large plant operated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wrangler_(Jeans)" title="Wrangler (Jeans)">Wrangler</a>. Most of the structures in downtown Hackleburg were badly damaged and Hackleburg High School was destroyed. Well-built homes were wiped cleanly from their foundations, extensive wind-rowing of debris occurred, trees were completely debarked, and cars were thrown hundreds of yards. According to the <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">Red Cross</a>, 75 percent of the town was destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> While initially rated as an EF3, the rating was increased to EF5 after further analysis of the damage, making it the first F5/EF5 tornado in Alabama since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_1998_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1998 Birmingham tornado">Birmingham tornado of April 8, 1998</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marion_survey_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marion_survey-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soon after crossing into <a href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_Alabama" title="Franklin County, Alabama">Franklin County</a>, the town of <a href="/wiki/Phil_Campbell,_Alabama" title="Phil Campbell, Alabama">Phil Campbell</a> experienced significant devastation of the same magnitude as Hackleburg. Numerous homes, some of which were well-constructed, were swept away as the tornado tore through town. At least three churches along the path sustained significant damage, with one church in the town being completely destroyed and having only the foundation slab remaining. Multiple mobile homes throughout the path were completely destroyed, and their mangled frames were tossed at least 25 to 50 yards (23 to 46 m). Cars were tossed and destroyed throughout the path of the tornado, with one car wrapped around a debarked tree. A 25-foot (7.6 m) section of pavement was torn from a road in this area as well. The most intense damage along the path occurred northeast of Phil Campbell in the rural community of Oak Grove, where vehicles were carried long distances and mangled beyond recognition, large trees were completely debarked, and large brick homes with extensive anchoring were obliterated with the debris wind-rowed hundreds of yards away. The tornado continued into <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_County,_Alabama" title="Lawrence County, Alabama">Lawrence County</a>, impacting the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Hope,_Lawrence_County,_Alabama" title="Mount Hope, Lawrence County, Alabama">Mount Hope</a> community, where significant devastation was incurred to single-family homes and a restaurant. Nothing but the foundation and a pile of debris remained at the restaurant site, and a small portion of the restaurant's foundation slab buckled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Huntsville_EF5_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Huntsville_EF5-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="675" data-file-width="900" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG/255px-PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG/383px-PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG/510px-PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PhilCampbellPavementScouring.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Large area of pavement scoured from a road in Phil Campbell.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The tornado moved northeast, producing EF3 damage in and around <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Langtown,_Alabama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Langtown, Alabama (page does not exist)">Langtown</a>. The tornado re-intensified to EF4 strength as it passed near <a href="/wiki/Moulton,_Alabama" title="Moulton, Alabama">Moulton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinity,_Alabama" title="Trinity, Alabama">Trinity</a>, debarking trees, mangling, and leveling homes. It then continued through the northwest corner of <a href="/wiki/Morgan_County,_Alabama" title="Morgan County, Alabama">Morgan County</a>, crossed Wheeler Lake, and moved into <a href="/wiki/Limestone_County,_Alabama" title="Limestone County, Alabama">Limestone County</a>, coming within 2 miles (3.2 km) of <a href="/wiki/Browns_Ferry_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Browns Ferry Nuclear Power Plant">Browns Ferry Nuclear Power Plant</a>. The tornado caused power outages in the area, and the plant had to be shut down. The tornado continued towards the small community of Tanner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS-HUN-SWS-04282141_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWS-HUN-SWS-04282141-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TFP-nuke_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-TFP-nuke-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUN-132.1mi_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-HUN-132.1mi-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tanner,_Alabama" title="Tanner, Alabama">Tanner</a> experienced a large swath of EF4 damage and a narrow corridor of "high-end EF4 to near-EF5 damage". The storm "completely wiped clean" several well constructed homes with anchor bolting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS-HUN-SWS-04282141_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-NWS-HUN-SWS-04282141-90">[90]</a></sup> As the storm crossed <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_72" title="U.S. Route 72">U.S. Highway 72</a> in eastern Limestone County, the tornado destroyed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doppler_weather_radar" title="Doppler weather radar">Doppler radar</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WAFF_(TV)" title="WAFF (TV)">WAFF</a> (channel 48) and continued into East Limestone, a heavily populated area of Limestone County where homes in multiple subdivisions were damaged or destroyed at high-end EF3 strength. As the storm crossed into Madison County, it approached the densely populated suburban communities of <a href="/wiki/Harvest,_Alabama" title="Harvest, Alabama">Harvest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toney,_Alabama" title="Toney, Alabama">Toney</a>, where it either damaged or destroyed hundreds of homes, especially in the Anderson Hills and Carter's Gin subdivisions. Many homes were reduced to rubble, and the damage in this area was rated mainly EF3 with a small pocket of EF4 damage in Harvest. The tornado completely destroyed a <a href="/wiki/Piggly_Wiggly" title="Piggly Wiggly">Piggly Wiggly</a> grocery store in Harvest and severely damaged a convenience store and local bank, which was shut down for months following the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWDJW-04272011ToneyHarvestDestruction_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-SWDJW-04272011ToneyHarvestDestruction-93">[93]</a></sup> The storm progressed across Pulaski Pike in northwest Madison County, damaging many homes. In all, hundreds of homes received moderate to major damage along the path from Limestone to Madison County with many of these being total losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS-HUN-SWS-04282141_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-NWS-HUN-SWS-04282141-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado then moved into <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> and continued south of <a href="/wiki/Huntland,_Tennessee" title="Huntland, Tennessee">Huntland</a>. Isolated and minor EF0 to EF1 damage was noted through most of its path in Tennessee. Widespread damage to trees and outbuildings occurred in this area. The worst damage, however, was to a cinder block utility building and was rated lower-end EF3. Most of its roof was removed, with over half of its downwind wall pushed outward. The tornado eventually dissipated east of Huntland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUN-132.1mi_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-HUN-132.1mi-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
