<p>In total, this tornado killed 72 people, all in Alabama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc_fatal_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-spc_fatal-2">[2]</a></sup> This made it the deadliest single tornado ever to strike the state of Alabama as well as (at the time) the deadliest in the United States since the 1955 <a href="/wiki/Udall,_Kansas" title="Udall, Kansas">Udall, Kansas</a> tornado that killed 80 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> In addition to being the deadliest, this tornado also had the longest track of any tornado in the outbreak, with its path extending 132.1 miles (212.6 km) across Northern Alabama and into Tennessee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HUN-132.1mi_92-2"><a href="#cite_note-HUN-132.1mi-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reform.E2.80.93Oakman.E2.80.93Cordova.E2.80.93Blountsville.2C_Alabama">Reform–Oakman–Cordova–Blountsville, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reform–Oakman–Cordova–Blountsville, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cordovafromwest.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Cordovafromwest.jpg/220px-Cordovafromwest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Cordovafromwest.jpg/330px-Cordovafromwest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Cordovafromwest.jpg/440px-Cordovafromwest.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cordovafromwest.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of the damage path through Cordova from the west (looking east).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The tornado touched down at 3:40 p.m. CDT (2040 UTC) in northeastern <a href="/wiki/Pickens_County,_Alabama" title="Pickens County, Alabama">Pickens County, Alabama</a>, damaging a few chicken homes, causing roof damage to houses, and destroying a few outbuildings before moving into <a href="/wiki/Tuscaloosa_County,_Alabama" title="Tuscaloosa County, Alabama">Tuscaloosa County</a> and briefly into <a href="/wiki/Fayette_County,_Alabama" title="Fayette County, Alabama">Fayette County</a>, where it caused minor structural damage. The tornado then moved back into Tuscaloosa County, causing mostly minor structural damage at EF1 strength before rapidly intensifying and crossing into Fayette County once again. There, it completely destroyed at least one mobile home, with the frame being separated and the remaining debris being thrown a considerable distance. The tornado strengthened even further, to EF3 intensity, and several mobile homes were obliterated with debris thrown a considerable distance and frames twisted and thrown. The tornado moved into <a href="/wiki/Walker_County,_Alabama" title="Walker County, Alabama">Walker County</a>, where it weakened to EF1 strength and caused minor roof damage to a mobile home and a site-built home. South of <a href="/wiki/Oakman,_Alabama" title="Oakman, Alabama">Oakman</a>, a cell phone tower was knocked down, and homes and mobile homes were destroyed at EF2 intensity. It then rolled vehicles and destroyed a cinder block house to the southeast of Oakman, with damage rated EF3 at that location. The tornado weakened considerably as it approached <a href="/wiki/Interstate_22" title="Interstate 22">Corridor X</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Development_Highway_System" title="Appalachian Development Highway System">Appalachian Development Highway System</a>, only downing a few trees, before it strengthened significantly as it entered the town of <a href="/wiki/Cordova,_Alabama" title="Cordova, Alabama">Cordova</a> as a 0.6-mile (0.97 km) wide EF3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordova_tornado_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cordova_tornado-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg/220px-CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg/330px-CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg/440px-CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CordovaDamagefromGround.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Major damage in a residential area of Cordova.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Considerable damage occurred as the tornado moved through Cordova, with numerous site-built homes and manufactured houses either being heavily damaged or destroyed. Buildings in downtown Cordova had already been damaged by an EF3 tornado earlier that morning and received further damage from this tornado. East of Cordova, the tornado crossed the <a href="/wiki/Mulberry_Fork_of_the_Black_Warrior_River" title="Mulberry Fork of the Black Warrior River">Mulberry Fork of the Black Warrior River</a> three times (along with the <a href="/wiki/Sipsey_Fork_of_the_Black_Warrior_River" title="Sipsey Fork of the Black Warrior River">Sipsey Fork</a> once, just north of its confluence with the Mulberry Fork). It intensified further into a violent EF4 in northeastern Walker County, and it completely leveled a site-built home and obliterated two nearby mobile homes. One of the mobile home undercarriages was tossed at least 500 yards (460 m). A small bulldozer was flipped over, a pickup truck was tossed 200 yards (180 m), and a dump truck was tossed 50 yards (46 m) and destroyed. A 2-short-ton (1,800 kg) trailer was found 1 mile (1.6 km) away, having left a 2.5-foot (0.76 m) deep crater where it impacted the ground. Two double-wide mobile homes were tossed at least 100 yards (91 m), and a third mobile home was tossed 100 yards (91 m) up a 50 foot (15 m) embankment and destroyed along this segment of the path as well. South of <a href="/wiki/Sipsey,_Alabama" title="Sipsey, Alabama">Sipsey</a>, multiple additional homes and mobile homes were destroyed at EF2 to EF3 strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordova_tornado_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cordova_tornado-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado then crossed the Mulberry Fork for the fourth time and moved into <a href="/wiki/Cullman_County,_Alabama" title="Cullman County, Alabama">Cullman County</a>. South of <a href="/wiki/Arkadelphia,_Alabama" title="Arkadelphia, Alabama">Arkadelphia</a>, a second area of EF4 damage was observed, as a cinder block construction home was leveled and a car was thrown 130 yards (120 m). Nearby, an underground storm shelter collapsed onto the occupants sheltering inside as the tornado passed overhead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordova_tornado_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cordova_tornado-96">[96]</a></sup> The tornado then crossed the Mulberry Fork again, moving into <a href="/wiki/Blount_County,_Alabama" title="Blount County, Alabama">Blount County</a> and causing roof damage to a home. It then crossed <a href="/wiki/Interstate_65_in_Alabama" title="Interstate 65 in Alabama">Interstate 65</a> before crossing the Mulberry Fork into Cullman County southwest of <a href="/wiki/Garden_City,_Alabama" title="Garden City, Alabama">Garden City</a>. It quickly crossed the river again (the seventh crossing), moving back into Blount County. As it continued to the south-southwest of Garden City, it straddled the Mulberry Fork before finally moving solidly into Blount County and toward <a href="/wiki/Blountsville,_Alabama" title="Blountsville, Alabama">Blountsville</a>. On the southeast side of Blountsville, the tornado caused high-end EF2 damage to multiple well-built brick and slab foundation homes, one of which had some exterior walls collapse. The storm continued to the northeast and out of Blountsville, where two additional homes sustained high-end EF3 damage. A large portion of one of the homes was wiped off of its foundation; however, its garage sustained only minor roof damage. At the second of these two homes, a dump truck was thrown 30 feet (9.1 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordova_tornado_96-3"><a href="#cite_note-Cordova_tornado-96">[96]</a></sup> The tornado then moved into <a href="/wiki/Marshall_County,_Alabama" title="Marshall County, Alabama">Marshall County</a>, causing significant damage to a house and downing numerous trees. A shed suffered roof damage and an industrial plant was completely destroyed at EF2 strength as well. The tornado then moved into a wooded area, weakened, and eventually lifted south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Guntersville,_Alabama" title="Guntersville, Alabama">Guntersville</a> at 5:56 p.m. CDT (2256 UTC). Thousands of trees were downed along the tornado's path.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_County_survey_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall_County_survey-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>This tornado was on the ground for two hours and sixteen minutes, tracking for 127.8 miles (205.7 km) across seven counties. It was rated as a low-end EF4 with winds of 170 mph (270 km/h). In total, 13 people were killed and 54 others were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cordova_tornado_96-4"><a href="#cite_note-Cordova_tornado-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marshall_County_survey_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall_County_survey-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smithville.2C_Mississippi.2FShottsville.2C_Alabama">Smithville, Mississippi/Shottsville, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Smithville, Mississippi/Shottsville, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Smithville,_Mississippi_tornado" title="2011 Smithville, Mississippi tornado">2011 Smithville, Mississippi tornado</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="491" data-file-width="960" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG/255px-Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG/383px-Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG/510px-Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Slab_Pulled_up_in_Smithville.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Extreme damage at a residence along Highway 25 near Smithville, with part of the foundation slab pulled up and dislodged slightly.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This extremely violent EF5 wedge tornado, with estimated winds of up to 205 mph (330 km/h), struck the town of <a href="/wiki/Smithville,_Mississippi" title="Smithville, Mississippi">Smithville, Mississippi</a> at 3:47 p.m. CDT (2047 UTC) on April 27, resulting in catastrophic damage and numerous fatalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSMemphisSmithvilleEF5_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSMemphisSmithvilleEF5-98">[98]</a></sup> The tornado began 3 miles (4.8 km) west-southwest of Smithville along the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee%E2%80%93Tombigbee_Waterway" title="Tennessee–Tombigbee Waterway">Tennessee–Tombigbee Waterway</a> near the <a href="/wiki/Glover_Wilkins_Lock" title="Glover Wilkins Lock">Glover Wilkins Lock</a> at 3:42 p.m. CDT (2042 UTC), snapping numerous trees near the Smithville Recreation Area. The tornado then rapidly intensified as it approached town, reaching EF5 intensity. As the storm crossed Davis Road South, the ground was deeply scoured in a nearby field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith._Damage_Imagery_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith._Damage_Imagery-99">[99]</a></sup> The tornado swept away numerous homes and structures as it moved northeast, following <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_Highway_25" title="Mississippi Highway 25">Highway 25</a>. A semi-truck was thrown a considerable distance and destroyed in this area, and at one residence that was swept away, part of the concrete foundation slab was pulled up and dislodged slightly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSMemphisSmithvilleEF5_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-NWSMemphisSmithvilleEF5-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith._Damage_Imagery_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-Smith._Damage_Imagery-99">[99]</a></sup> A large brick funeral home was reduced to a bare slab as the tornado exited at the northeast side of town, with the debris scattered and wind-rowed into an adjacent wooded area. Nearby granite tombstones were blown over in the opposite direction of the tornado's passage. Overall, the tornado destroyed 117 structures in Smithville and damaged 50 others, killing 16 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smithville_NCDC_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smithville_NCDC-100">[100]</a></sup> The tornado weakened as it continued through rural areas northeast of town and moved into <a href="/wiki/Itawamba_County,_Mississippi" title="Itawamba County, Mississippi">Itawamba County</a>, where it downed numerous trees and power lines and caused roof damage to a house before exiting the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith._Damage_Imagery_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-Smith._Damage_Imagery-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado continued across the <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a> state line into <a href="/wiki/Marion_County,_Alabama" title="Marion County, Alabama">Marion County</a>, where it caused EF1-strength damage near <a href="/wiki/Bexar,_Alabama" title="Bexar, Alabama">Bexar</a>. Continuing northeast, the tornado re-intensified as it struck the rural community of <a href="/wiki/Shottsville,_Alabama" title="Shottsville, Alabama">Shottsville</a> at high-end EF3 intensity, where homes and mobile homes were destroyed and seven people were killed, and it produced additional high-end EF3 damage as it continued north of <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Alabama" title="Hamilton, Alabama">Hamilton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-102">[102]</a></sup> More structures were impacted as the tornado approached and crossed into <a href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_Alabama" title="Franklin County, Alabama">Franklin County</a>. The tornado then dissipated near the town of <a href="/wiki/Hodges,_Alabama" title="Hodges, Alabama">Hodges</a> at 4:23 p.m. CDT (2123 UTC). The damage path was 37.3 miles (60.0 km) long and <span class="frac nowrap"><sup>3</sup>⁄<sub>4</sub></span> mile (1.2 km) wide at its widest point, and it killed a total of 23 people along its path. 137 other people were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pisgah.E2.80.93Flat_Rock.E2.80.93Higdon.2C_Alabama.2FTrenton.2C_Georgia">Pisgah–Flat Rock–Higdon, Alabama/Trenton, Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Pisgah–Flat Rock–Higdon, Alabama/Trenton, Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:257px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trenton2011.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Trenton2011.JPG/255px-Trenton2011.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Trenton2011.JPG/383px-Trenton2011.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Trenton2011.JPG/510px-Trenton2011.JPG 2x" width="255"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trenton2011.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of damage in Trenton.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This multiple-vortex EF4 tornado devastated portions of <a href="/wiki/Jackson_County,_Alabama" title="Jackson County, Alabama">Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/DeKalb_County,_Alabama" title="DeKalb County, Alabama">DeKalb</a> counties in Alabama, as well as <a href="/wiki/Dade_County,_Georgia" title="Dade County, Georgia">Dade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walker_County,_Georgia" title="Walker County, Georgia">Walker</a> counties in Georgia along a 47-mile long path, killing 14 people and injuring at least 50 others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Events_Database_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Events_Database-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc.noaa.gov_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc.noaa.gov-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado touched down north of <a href="/wiki/Section,_Alabama" title="Section, Alabama">Section</a>, initially producing EF0 to EF1 tree damage. The tornado rapidly intensified to low-end EF4 strength as it passed northwest of <a href="/wiki/Pisgah,_Alabama" title="Pisgah, Alabama">Pisgah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rosalie,_Alabama" title="Rosalie, Alabama">Rosalie</a>, destroying numerous mobile homes and block foundation homes, scattering the debris hundreds of yards and killing three people. Thousands of trees were snapped and debarked, vehicles were thrown up to 50 yards in different directions, and multiple barns and chicken houses were heavily damaged, along with the roof of a church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-104">[104]</a></sup> As it passed near <a href="/wiki/Flat_Rock,_Alabama" title="Flat Rock, Alabama">Flat Rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Higdon,_Alabama" title="Higdon, Alabama">Higdon</a>, the tornado reached high-end EF4 strength, mowing down thousands of trees in this rural area. As the tornado struck a farm, a home and two chicken houses were completely obliterated and swept away. A heavy propane tank was lofted and thrown 100 yards from one of the chicken houses, and 19 cattle on the property were killed. Remarkably, a family of four taking shelter inside the house were completely unharmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-104">[104]</a></sup> The tornado maintained EF4 strength as it tore through the rural community of Shiloh, sweeping away numerous mobile homes and block foundation homes and killing 5 people at that location. Thousands of trees were snapped, a log cabin was destroyed, livestock was killed, chicken houses were flattened, and a van was lofted and dropped into a field 400 yards away from where it originated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_104-3"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-104">[104]</a></sup> The tornado then crossed into Georgia and struck <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_Georgia" title="Trenton, Georgia">Trenton</a> as an EF3, killing two people. Dozens of homes in Trenton were completely destroyed, 18 others sustained major damage, and tens of thousands of trees were downed in the area. A grocery store, two apartment complexes, and a funeral home were destroyed as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Events_Database_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Events_Database-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado weakened to EF2 strength as it struck <a href="/wiki/Flintstone,_Georgia" title="Flintstone, Georgia">Flintstone</a> further to the northeast, but still resulted in major damage. Numerous trees and power lines were downed, 7 homes were destroyed, 26 sustained major damage, and 35 sustained minor damage in the Flintstone area. The tornado continued northeast, weakening to EF0 strength and dissipating in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Oglethorpe,_Georgia" title="Fort Oglethorpe, Georgia">Fort Oglethorpe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncdc.noaa.gov_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncdc.noaa.gov-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuscaloosa.2FBirmingham.2C_Alabama">Tuscaloosa/Birmingham, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tuscaloosa/Birmingham, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Tuscaloosa%E2%80%93Birmingham_tornado" title="2011 Tuscaloosa–Birmingham tornado">2011 Tuscaloosa–Birmingham tornado</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa,_Alabama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6420" data-file-width="3868" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa%2C_Alabama.jpg/170px-Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa%2C_Alabama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa%2C_Alabama.jpg/255px-Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa%2C_Alabama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa%2C_Alabama.jpg/340px-Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa%2C_Alabama.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tornado_Track_in_Tuscaloosa,_Alabama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite image of the tornado's track through Tuscaloosa.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A large multiple-vortex <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wedge_tornado" title="Wedge tornado">wedge tornado</a> touched down in rural <a href="/wiki/Greene_County,_Alabama" title="Greene County, Alabama">Greene County, Alabama</a> and tracked across neighboring <a href="/wiki/Tuscaloosa_County,_Alabama" title="Tuscaloosa County, Alabama">Tuscaloosa County</a>, including the southern and eastern portions of <a href="/wiki/Tuscaloosa,_Alabama" title="Tuscaloosa, Alabama">Tuscaloosa</a> at around 5:10 p.m. CDT (2210 UTC) on April 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-massive_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-massive-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey-107">[107]</a></sup> Debris from the tornado was reported to be falling from the sky across <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham</a> over 20 miles (32 km) away in <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Alabama" title="Jefferson County, Alabama">Jefferson County</a>. Skycams operated by Tuscaloosa television station <a href="/wiki/WVUA-CD" title="WVUA-CD">WVUA-CA</a> (channel 7) as well as Birmingham <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WBRC" title="WBRC">WBRC</a> (channel 6), <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> affiliate WBMA-LD/WCFT-TV/WJSU-TV (channels 58, 33, and 40), and <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WIAT" title="WIAT">WIAT</a> (channel 42) captured video of the tornado as it struck Tuscaloosa (WIAT took home multiple awards including a regional <a href="/wiki/Edward_R._Murrow_Award_(Radio_Television_Digital_News_Association)" title="Edward R. Murrow Award (Radio Television Digital News Association)">Edward R. Murrow Award</a> for "outstanding live coverage" of the event).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> As the tornado traveled east to 35th Street and Kauloosa Avenue, the Tuscaloosa Environmental Services and <a href="/wiki/Cintas" title="Cintas">Cintas</a> facilities suffered severe damage. Numerous homes and apartment buildings in the Rosedale and Forest Lake neighborhoods, as well as a P&amp;P Grocery store in Rosedale, were devastated. Several stores and restaurants in a business district at the intersection of McFarland Boulevard and 15th Street, near the DCH Regional Medical Center, were reduced to rubble by the tornado. Buildings were also completely destroyed on 35th Street, between <a href="/wiki/Interstate_359" title="Interstate 359">Interstate 359</a> and Martin Luther King Jr. Boulevard. The Alberta City neighborhood in eastern Tuscaloosa sustained catastrophic damage as numerous homes, apartment buildings, and a shopping center were completely leveled. Additional high-end EF4 damage occurred in the Tuscaloosa suburb of <a href="/wiki/Holt,_Alabama" title="Holt, Alabama">Holt</a> further to the northeast, as several homes were leveled or swept away in that area. The tornado then exited the Tuscaloosa area and moved through dense forest towards Birmingham, downing and debarking thousands of trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama" title="University of Alabama">University of Alabama</a> suspended its operations, cancelled its softball and rowing competitions, cancelled its final exams period, and postponed its commencement until August 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG/220px-Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG/330px-Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG/440px-Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tuscaloosa_Apartment_Complex.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The demolished Chastain Manor apartment complex in Tuscaloosa.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many stations, including WIAT, WBMA/WCFT/WJSU, <a href="/wiki/WTVY_(TV)" title="WTVY (TV)">WTVY</a> (channel 4) in <a href="/wiki/Dothan,_Alabama" title="Dothan, Alabama">Dothan</a> and <a href="/wiki/WSFA" title="WSFA">WSFA</a> (channel 12) in <a href="/wiki/Montgomery,_Alabama" title="Montgomery, Alabama">Montgomery</a>, showed television cameras capturing the event as the tornado moved east-northeast across the western and northern suburbs of Birmingham around 6:00 p.m. CDT (2300 UTC). Several suburbs in the area were severely damaged by the massive tornado as it tore through the west side of Birmingham, resulting in multiple fatalities. The suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Concord,_Alabama" title="Concord, Alabama">Concord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pleasant_Grove,_Alabama" title="Pleasant Grove, Alabama">Pleasant Grove</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McDonald_Chapel,_Alabama" title="McDonald Chapel, Alabama">McDonald Chapel</a> were devastated by the tornado as it moved northeast, flattening entire neighborhoods. As the tornado entered the Birmingham city limits, it devastated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pratt_City,_Alabama" title="Pratt City, Alabama">Pratt City</a> neighborhood, destroying numerous homes and apartment buildings. The tornado then struck the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Fultondale,_Alabama" title="Fultondale, Alabama">Fultondale</a>, causing EF2 damage to homes and businesses before dissipating east of Fultondale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Surveys indicated high-end EF4 damage from the tornado in Birmingham's western suburbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey_107-2"><a href="#cite_note-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> determined the path length of this violent tornado to be 80.7 miles (129.9 km) with a maximum damage path width of 1.5 miles (2.4 km). The tornado's most intense damage indicated peak winds of around 190 mph (310 km/h); therefore, it was given a final rating of EF4. Reports from Tuscaloosa indicated 44 people were killed, with an additional 20 deaths in Birmingham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey_107-3"><a href="#cite_note-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Overall this tornado killed 64 people and injured more than 1500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc_fatal_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-spc_fatal-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey_107-4"><a href="#cite_note-NWSBir.Tusc.Survey-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady</a> <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle Obama</a> visited Tuscaloosa on April 29, taking a ground tour of some of the affected areas. Obama was quoted as saying that he has "never seen devastation like this." He stated further that he had already declared a federal state of emergency in Alabama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nprttown_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-nprttown-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fackler.E2.80.93Stevenson.E2.80.93Bridgeport.2C_Alabama.2FHaletown.2C_Tennessee">Fackler–Stevenson–Bridgeport, Alabama/Haletown, Tennessee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fackler–Stevenson–Bridgeport, Alabama/Haletown, Tennessee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport,_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="623" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Bridgeport%2C_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg/220px-Bridgeport%2C_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Bridgeport%2C_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg/330px-Bridgeport%2C_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Bridgeport%2C_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg/440px-Bridgeport%2C_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bridgeport,_AL_April_27_tornado_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Concrete steps that were ripped from the foundation of a house, with a small concrete porch slab pulled up in the background.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This EF4 tornado, with winds of up to 180 mph (290 km/h), touched down just northeast of the community of <a href="/wiki/Fackler,_Alabama" title="Fackler, Alabama">Fackler</a> at 5:05 p.m. CDT (2205 UTC) on April 27, initially causing minor damage to mobile homes and downing trees. The tornado then moved northeast toward <a href="/wiki/Stevenson,_Alabama" title="Stevenson, Alabama">Stevenson</a>, where large trees were downed, several roofs were damaged, a trailer was tipped over, and a shed was partially destroyed. It then reached EF3 intensity, and 24 metal high-tension truss towers were twisted and flattened northeast of <a href="/wiki/Stevenson_Airport" title="Stevenson Airport">Stevenson Airport</a>. In this area, a mobile home was obliterated and a site-built house was collapsed. Two other homes sustained structural damage, two mobile homes were rolled on their side, and a metal barn was destroyed as well. The tornado then continued to the northeast and reached EF4 strength, with the most significant damage being located near the intersection of County Roads 255 and 256. Here, a home was reduced to its foundation, a concrete slab at the front of the home was pulled up, and a set of concrete stairs was ripped from the foundation. A compact car was thrown about 50 yards (46 m) as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fackler_tornado_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fackler_tornado-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FacklerNCDC_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FacklerNCDC-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Continuing, the tornado reduced two more well-built and well-anchored homes to their block foundations and threw another car approximately 50 yards (46 m). Several large trees were snapped off just above the ground, a third home was left with no walls standing, and a mobile home was completely demolished and strewn along County Road 256 as well. The tornado continued northeastward, destroying a cinder block garage and damaging a mobile home along 6th Street, just southeast of <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_Alabama" title="Bridgeport, Alabama">Bridgeport</a>. It then crossed the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_River" title="Tennessee River">Tennessee River</a>, producing significant tree damage before moving into <a href="/wiki/Marion_County,_Tennessee" title="Marion County, Tennessee">Marion County, Tennessee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fackler_tornado_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fackler_tornado-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FacklerNCDC_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-FacklerNCDC-115">[115]</a></sup> The tornado entered <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> along Lakeview Drive near <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Moore_Crossing,_Tennessee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Moore Crossing, Tennessee (page does not exist)">Moore Crossing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nickajack_Dam" title="Nickajack Dam">Nickajack Dam</a>. It then proceeded to cross <a href="/wiki/Nickajack_Lake" title="Nickajack Lake">Nickajack Lake</a> three times near <a href="/wiki/Interstate_24" title="Interstate 24">Interstate 24</a> at EF2 strength, downing numerous trees before dissipating in a bend of the Tennessee River northeast of <a href="/wiki/Haletown,_Tennessee" title="Haletown, Tennessee">Haletown</a> at 5:31 p.m. CDT (2231 UTC). The tornado travelled 30.24 miles (48.67 km) through Jackson and Marion Counties and had a peak width of 1,320 yards (1,210 m). One person was killed by the tornado in Jackson County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fackler_tornado_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-Fackler_tornado-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FacklerNCDC_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-FacklerNCDC-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sawyerville.E2.80.93Eoline.2C_Alabama">Sawyerville–Eoline, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sawyerville–Eoline, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This strong, long-tracked wedge tornado touched down in extreme southwest <a href="/wiki/Greene_County,_Alabama" title="Greene County, Alabama">Greene County</a> to the west-southwest of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tishabee,_Alabama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tishabee, Alabama (page does not exist)">Tishabee</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Sumter_County,_Alabama" title="Sumter County, Alabama">Sumter County</a> border, at 5:30 p.m. CDT (2230 UTC) and moved northeast. After having touched down in a rural area on the east side of the <a href="/wiki/Tombigbee_River" title="Tombigbee River">Tombigbee River</a>, the tornado quickly intensified to high-end EF2 strength along County Road 69. Moving northeast, the tornado damaged a barn and destroyed two small churches and at least four mobile homes. While crossing <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_43" title="U.S. Route 43">U.S. Highway 43</a>, the tornado destroyed a large metal outbuilding, caused substantial roof and wall damage to several brick buildings and homes. Hundreds of trees were downed in this area as well. Two people sustained minor injuries in Greene County as the tornado continued along a primarily rural path northeast, moving across the <a href="/wiki/Black_Warrior_River" title="Black Warrior River">Black Warrior River</a> and into <a href="/wiki/Hale_County,_Alabama" title="Hale County, Alabama">Hale County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreeneCo_NCDC_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-GreeneCo_NCDC-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado entered Hale County west of <a href="/wiki/Sawyerville,_Alabama" title="Sawyerville, Alabama">Sawyerville</a>, continuing to move through sparsely populated rural areas. North of Sawyerville, the tornado strengthened to EF3 intensity as it was crossing <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_14" title="Alabama State Route 14">Alabama State Highway 14</a>. Reaching estimated maximum winds of 145 mph (233 km/h), the tornado continued on its northeast track, crossing County Roads 18 and 21, <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_69" title="Alabama State Route 69">Alabama State Highway 69</a>, and County Road 29 as it moved south and east of the small communities of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Harper_Hill,_Alabama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Harper Hill, Alabama (page does not exist)">Harper Hill</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ingram,_Alabama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ingram, Alabama (page does not exist)">Ingram</a>. The tornado caused extensive structural damage through this area, consisting of many mobile homes and site-built homes being either heavily damaged or destroyed. A church in the area was heavily damaged, vehicles were tossed and destroyed, and thousands of trees were downed as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaleCoEF3_NCDC_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-HaleCoEF3_NCDC-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EolineFireDept.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/EolineFireDept.jpg/220px-EolineFireDept.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/EolineFireDept.jpg/330px-EolineFireDept.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/EolineFireDept.jpg/440px-EolineFireDept.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EolineFireDept.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The destroyed Eoline Volunteer Fire Department building.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Leaving behind six fatalities and forty more injuries, the tornado maintained its intensity as it moved into the <a href="/wiki/Talladega_National_Forest" title="Talladega National Forest">Talladega National Forest</a>. It downed a significant number of trees before moving into <a href="/wiki/Bibb_County,_Alabama" title="Bibb County, Alabama">Bibb County</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_25" title="Alabama State Route 25">Alabama State Highway 25</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaleCoEF3_NCDC_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-HaleCoEF3_NCDC-119">[119]</a></sup> In Bibb County, the tornado continued moving northeastward through the Talladega National Forest at EF3 intensity, with thousands more trees being knocked down and partially debarked. Almost immediately after exiting the national forest, the tornado directly impacted the small community of <a href="/wiki/Eoline,_Alabama" title="Eoline, Alabama">Eoline</a> along <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_82" title="U.S. Route 82">U.S. Highway 82</a>, northwest of <a href="/wiki/Brent,_Alabama" title="Brent, Alabama">Brent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Centerville,_Alabama" title="Centerville, Alabama">Centerville</a>. Around one dozen mobile homes and single-family site-built homes were destroyed, while many more sustained anywhere from minor to major damage. Additionally, the Eoline Volunteer Fire Department and another business were destroyed. One fatality occurred in Eoline, in a vehicle near the fire department building, along with ten other injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado_117-3"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BibbCoEF3_NCDC_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-BibbCoEF3_NCDC-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Northeast of Eoline, the tornado weakened to EF2 intensity, continuing to cause significant damage as it crossed County Road 9, <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_5" title="Alabama State Route 5">Alabama State Highway 5</a>, and County Road 26, south of <a href="/wiki/West_Blocton,_Alabama" title="West Blocton, Alabama">West Blocton</a>. Several mobile homes and site-built homes were either destroyed or sustained major damage. Along the path, thousands of trees were downed. The tornado continued to weaken as it moved to the east of West Blocton, continuing to knock down trees. More trees were downed as the tornado crossed the <a href="/wiki/Cahaba_River" title="Cahaba River">Cahaba River</a> and lifted just northeast of <a href="/wiki/Marvel,_Alabama" title="Marvel, Alabama">Marvel</a> at 6:55 p.m. CDT (2355 UTC), not far from the <a href="/wiki/Shelby_County,_Alabama" title="Shelby County, Alabama">Shelby County</a> border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado_117-4"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BibbCoEF3_NCDC_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-BibbCoEF3_NCDC-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado was rated as an EF3, with maximum sustained winds of 145 mph (233 km/h). It remained on the ground for almost an hour and a half, traversing 72.13 miles (116.08 km), being, at times, about 1 mile (1.6 km) wide. In total, seven people were killed and an additional 52 were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado_117-5"><a href="#cite_note-Sawyerville.2FEoline_tornado-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreeneCo_NCDC_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-GreeneCo_NCDC-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HaleCoEF3_NCDC_119-2"><a href="#cite_note-HaleCoEF3_NCDC-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BibbCoEF3_NCDC_120-2"><a href="#cite_note-BibbCoEF3_NCDC-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Raleigh.E2.80.93Rose_Hill.E2.80.93Enterprise.2C_Mississippi.2FYantley.E2.80.93Uniontown.2C_Alabama">Raleigh–Rose Hill–Enterprise, Mississippi/Yantley–Uniontown, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Raleigh–Rose Hill–Enterprise, Mississippi/Yantley–Uniontown, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="725" data-file-width="967" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg/220px-Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg/330px-Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg/440px-Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smith_Jasper_Clarke_Counties_tornado_2011-04-27.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Photo of the EF4 Enterprise tornado as it was in southeast Mississippi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado-121">[121]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This extremely long-tracked EF4 tornado touched down near <a href="/wiki/Raleigh,_Mississippi" title="Raleigh, Mississippi">Raleigh, Mississippi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Smith_County,_Mississippi" title="Smith County, Mississippi">Smith County</a> at 5:42 p.m. CDT (2242 UTC), and continued into the <a href="/wiki/Uniontown,_Alabama" title="Uniontown, Alabama">Uniontown, Alabama</a> area before dissipating. The tornado initially downed trees, blew skirting from mobile homes, and tore shingles from roofs. The tornado intensified as it moved northeast across Smith County and produced up to EF2 and EF3 damage. One mobile home was picked up, bounced a couple times, and thrown into a tree line, where it was torn apart and debris was scattered up to a mile away, including the frame. The tornado mowed down a stand of pine trees and destroyed two frame houses, with major damage to the interior walls, and the exterior walls completely destroyed. Many power poles were snapped, a mobile home was annihilated, and a large shop building was completely destroyed as well. It then moved into <a href="/wiki/Jasper_County,_Mississippi" title="Jasper County, Mississippi">Jasper County</a> and snapped and debarked many pine trees. The first area of EF4 damage was observed near <a href="/wiki/Louin,_Mississippi" title="Louin, Mississippi">Louin</a> as a frame home and several mobile homes were completely destroyed, with parts of the mobile homes being thrown long distances, and some of the frame home foundation being swept clean. The tornado caused significant damage to a poultry farm and cattle ranch before it weakened briefly. It then destroyed two mobile homes and caused extensive tree and power line damage. The tornado then produced a relatively narrow path of EF1-strength tree and power line damage for several miles, until re-intensifying near to EF3 strength near <a href="/wiki/Rose_Hill,_Jasper_County,_Mississippi" title="Rose Hill, Jasper County, Mississippi">Rose Hill</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Southeast of Rose Hill, the tornado removed most of the roof of a frame home and caused heavy damage to the exterior walls, took a large section of roof off another frame home, completely destroyed a large mobile home, and caused extensive tree damage. The tornado then weakened again and entered <a href="/wiki/Clarke_County,_Mississippi" title="Clarke County, Mississippi">Clarke County</a> as an EF0 while only downing a few trees. The tornado strengthened again and downed trees and power lines as it crossed <a href="/wiki/Interstate_59" title="Interstate 59">Interstate 59</a>. Several other homes and mobile homes were destroyed as the tornado moved along the south side of <a href="/wiki/Enterprise,_Mississippi" title="Enterprise, Mississippi">Enterprise</a>. At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Casey_(filmmaker)" title="Sean Casey (filmmaker)">Sean Casey</a> of Team TIV shot the tornado with his new 3D camera as it was crossing I-59, making this the first tornado ever shot in 3D. Another area of EF4 damage was observed east of Enterprise as a new home undergoing completion was leveled, with the debris swept off the foundation. Many more frame homes were heavily damaged nearby. Many mobile homes were destroyed and trees were downed in this area as well. It then weakened slightly to EF3 strength and produced heavy damage to more houses and mobile homes near <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Snell,_Mississippi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Snell, Mississippi (page does not exist)">Snell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy,_Mississippi" title="Energy, Mississippi">Energy</a>. It also downed many more trees and power lines before moving into <a href="/wiki/Choctaw_County,_Alabama" title="Choctaw County, Alabama">Choctaw County, Alabama</a> southwest of <a href="/wiki/Yantley,_Alabama" title="Yantley, Alabama">Yantley</a>. The tornado killed seven people and injured fourteen others on its 65-mile (105 km) portion of the path that was in <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado_121-2"><a href="#cite_note-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Choctaw County, the tornado traveled 27.5 miles (44.3 km) as it caused extensive damage to homes (one of which was destroyed at EF3 strength), and numerous other structures. Several mobile homes were destroyed and many trees were either snapped or completely uprooted. The tornado then moved into <a href="/wiki/Sumter_County,_Alabama" title="Sumter County, Alabama">Sumter County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yantley_survey_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yantley_survey-122">[122]</a></sup> In Sumter County, the tornado caused significant damage to homes and mobile homes before it crossed the <a href="/wiki/Tombigbee_River" title="Tombigbee River">Tombigbee River</a> and moved into <a href="/wiki/Marengo_County,_Alabama" title="Marengo County, Alabama">Marengo County</a>. It continued causing significant tree damage as well as destroying several homes and outbuildings along a 26.7-mile (43.0 km) path in this county. The tornado then entered <a href="/wiki/Perry_County,_Alabama" title="Perry County, Alabama">Perry County</a>, the final portion of the path, where it damaged two outbuildings and a grain silo as well as causing significant tree damage before lifting just north of <a href="/wiki/Uniontown,_Alabama" title="Uniontown, Alabama">Uniontown</a> at 8:35 p.m. CDT (0135 UTC). The damage in Sumter, Marengo, and Perry Counties was rated EF2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uniontown_tornado_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Uniontown_tornado-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>This tornado was on the ground for nearly three hours, having traveled 122.04 miles (196.40 km) across seven counties in two states. Seven people were killed and another 17 were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado_121-3"><a href="#cite_note-Raleigh.2C_MS_tornado-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yantley_survey_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yantley_survey-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uniontown_tornado_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-Uniontown_tornado-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fyffe.E2.80.93Rainsville.E2.80.93Sylvania.E2.80.93Ider.2C_Alabama">Fyffe–Rainsville–Sylvania–Ider, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fyffe–Rainsville–Sylvania–Ider, Alabama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG/220px-Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG/330px-Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG/440px-Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_bus_in_Rainsville.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
School bus stripped down to its chassis in Rainsville.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This violent multiple-vortex tornado, rated EF5, devastated sections of <a href="/wiki/DeKalb_County,_Alabama" title="DeKalb County, Alabama">DeKalb County, Alabama</a> at 6:19 p.m. CDT (2319 UTC), during the late afternoon of April 27. The tornado tracked northeastward generally parallel to and just east of <a href="/wiki/Alabama_State_Route_75" title="Alabama State Route 75">Highway 75</a> through <a href="/wiki/Fyffe,_Alabama" title="Fyffe, Alabama">Fyffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rainsville,_Alabama" title="Rainsville, Alabama">Rainsville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sylvania,_Alabama" title="Sylvania, Alabama">Sylvania</a> and into <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, killing 25 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado touched down in the Lakeview community, initially causing structural damage to small buildings and snapping trees. The tornado grew in intensity as it struck Fyffe, where more significant damage occurred. Past Fyffe, the tornado became violent, and its width increased from around 50 yards (46 m) to 0.5 miles (800 m) as it entered eastern Rainsville, reaching EF5 strength and destroying numerous homes and businesses. A <a href="/wiki/Huddle_House" title="Huddle House">Huddle House</a> restaurant, the Rainsville Civic Center, and a credit union were destroyed. Multiple vehicles were also thrown, including a school bus that was completely stripped down to its chassis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Numerous homes in the Rainsville area were swept completely away, with debris strewn up to a mile from the foundations. Some of these homes were connected to their foundations with anchor bolts and foundation straps. Trees were debarked and mobile homes were completely destroyed as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey-124">[124]</a></sup> Damage was particularly intense just northeast of Rainsville, and one well-built stone house in this area was completely obliterated, with the debris strewn well away from the structure. A large supporting cement and stone pillar was ripped completely out of the ground at this residence, pulling up a section of concrete foundation in the process. Scouring and pock-marking of the ground was noted in this area. Numerous homes were swept away along Lingerfelt Rd as well. At one house that was swept away in this area, supporting concrete anchors were ripped out of the ground, a concrete porch was ripped off with pieces strewn up to 150 yards (140 m) away, a pick-up truck from the home was found mangled in pieces over 250 yards (230 m) away, and a safe weighing 800 pounds (360 kg) was pulled off its anchorage and thrown into a wooded area 600 feet (180 m) away. When found, the safe's door had been ripped open and completely off.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey_124-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey-124">[124]</a></sup> An underground storm shelter in this area had much of its dirt covering scoured away, the occupants of which reported that structure heaved upwards slightly as the tornado passed overhead. Pavement was scoured from several roads in the area, and a concrete porch was torn away and broken in half at another residence that was swept away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado continued across the eastern fringes of Sylvania, where a church was completely destroyed, a section of sidewalk was pulled up, and additional homes were swept away and scattered, though it was revealed that these homes were pushed off of their foundations with limited anchorage. A high-end EF4 rating was applied in this area as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey_124-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey-124">[124]</a></sup> The tornado continued to level additional homes as it passed near <a href="/wiki/Henagar,_Alabama" title="Henagar, Alabama">Henegar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ider,_Alabama" title="Ider, Alabama">Ider</a>. It crossed into <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> near <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fox_Mountain,_Georgia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fox Mountain, Georgia (page does not exist)">Fox Mountain</a> as an EF1 with winds of 110 mph (180 km/h). It tracked 3 miles (4.8 km) into Georgia before lifting outside of <a href="/wiki/Rising_Fawn,_Georgia" title="Rising Fawn, Georgia">Rising Fawn</a>. Damage in Georgia was limited to trees and power lines and minor structural damage to a few homes. This tornado came from the same supercell that produced the EF4 that hit the town of <a href="/wiki/Ringgold,_Georgia" title="Ringgold, Georgia">Ringgold, Georgia</a> about 30 minutes later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey_124-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rainsville.2C_AL_Tornado_Survey-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shoal_Creek_Valley.E2.80.93Ohatchee.E2.80.93Piedmont.2C_Alabama.2FCave_Spring.2C_Georgia">Shoal Creek Valley–Ohatchee–Piedmont, Alabama/Cave Spring, Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Shoal Creek Valley–Ohatchee–Piedmont, Alabama/Cave Spring, Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27,_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="502" data-file-width="662" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27%2C_2011.jpg/220px-Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27%2C_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27%2C_2011.jpg/330px-Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27%2C_2011.jpg/440px-Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27%2C_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shoal_Creek_Valley_Alabama_Tornado_April_27,_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Shoal Creek Valley/Ohatchee EF4 tornado.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Tuscaloosa/Birmingham tornado lifted, the same supercell produced another tornado, at 6:28 p.m. CDT (2328 UTC) near <a href="/wiki/Argo,_Alabama" title="Argo, Alabama">Argo, Alabama</a> in eastern <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Alabama" title="Jefferson County, Alabama">Jefferson County</a>. It went on to devastate the rural community of Shoal Creek Valley, located between <a href="/wiki/Ashville,_Alabama" title="Ashville, Alabama">Ashville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ragland,_Alabama" title="Ragland, Alabama">Ragland</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Clair_County,_Alabama" title="St. Clair County, Alabama">St. Clair County, Alabama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>After touching down southwest of Argo, the tornado continued northeast of <a href="/wiki/Odenville,_Alabama" title="Odenville, Alabama">Odenville</a>, producing EF0 to EF1 tree damage. Further east, the tornado intensified to EF3 strength and entered the rural community of Shoal Creek Valley, following along County Road 22/Shoal Creek Road for approximately 12.5 miles (20.1 km), with the path and width varying greatly along the road. Many homes were left with only interior walls standing in this area. Some section of this path segment had damage that was much worse on one side of the road than the other, while other areas showed equal devastation on both sides of the road. The tornado reached mid-range EF4 intensity towards the end of the valley as it approached <a href="/wiki/Neely_Henry_Lake" title="Neely Henry Lake">Neely Henry Lake</a>. Additional homes were destroyed in this area, one was swept away, and thousands of trees were mowed down and debarked. The tornado maintained EF4 strength as it crossed the lake and tore across the north edge of <a href="/wiki/Ohatchee,_Alabama" title="Ohatchee, Alabama">Ohatchee</a>, completely leveling or sweeping away numerous waterfront homes. Damage ranged from downed trees and roof damage to total destruction as the tornado roared through this area at 50–60 mph (80–97 km/h), packing winds of over 180 mph (290 km/h). The official count of homes destroyed or heavily damaged in Shoal Creek Valley and Ohatchee was 256. Most phone lines, power lines and poles were destroyed, and water lines were severed by uprooted trees. Entire homes were leveled, and in some cases completely removed by the storm, leaving only brick steps, a fireplace and chimney, or a slab behind. Barns, vehicles, tractors and heavy farming equipment were shredded and thrown up to 0.5 miles (0.80 km) away from where they originated. Livestock were thrown and killed, and the initial human death toll of 13 would eventually rise to 15 in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey-128">[128]</a></sup> The tornado caused mainly EF3 damage to homes as it passed north of <a href="/wiki/Wellington,_Alabama" title="Wellington, Alabama">Wellington</a>, though a small pocket of EF4 damage occurred in the small rural community of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Webster%27s_Chapel,_Alabama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Webster's Chapel, Alabama (page does not exist)">Webster's Chapel</a>, where a church and several homes were completely leveled or swept away, trees were reduced to stumps, and many other homes were left with only interior walls standing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey_128-2"><a href="#cite_note-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The Silver Lakes Golf Course also sustained major damage in this area, where at least 50,000 trees were flattened and multiple buildings were damaged or destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Continuing northeast, the tornado produced high-end EF3 damage north of <a href="/wiki/Piedmont,_Alabama" title="Piedmont, Alabama">Piedmont</a>, destroying mobile homes, snapping numerous trees, and leveling a house. Additional homes were leveled at high-end EF3 intensity near <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Indian_Mountain_Tract&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Indian Mountain Tract (page does not exist)">The Indian Mountain Tract</a> before it continued across rural areas into <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey_128-3"><a href="#cite_note-Shoal_Creek-Ohatchee_survey-128">[128]</a></sup> Many outbuildings and homes were destroyed, and many trees were downed across <a href="/wiki/Polk_County,_Georgia" title="Polk County, Georgia">Polk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floyd_County,_Georgia" title="Floyd County, Georgia">Floyd</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bartow_County,_Georgia" title="Bartow County, Georgia">Bartow</a> counties before the tornado dissipated. Severe damage was noted near <a href="/wiki/Cave_Spring,_Georgia" title="Cave Spring, Georgia">Cave Spring</a> where chicken houses and homes were damaged or destroyed, and several people were injured. The damage in Georgia was rated EF2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>This tornado's final death toll, combining fatalities in both St. Clair and <a href="/wiki/Calhoun_County,_Alabama" title="Calhoun County, Alabama">Calhoun</a> counties in Alabama, would eventually come to 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spc_fatal_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-spc_fatal-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ringgold.2C_Georgia.2FSoutheast_Tennessee">Ringgold, Georgia/Southeast Tennessee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ringgold, Georgia/Southeast Tennessee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg/220px-Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg/330px-Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg/440px-Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringgold_tornado_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
EF4 damage in a subdivision at the north edge of Ringgold, GA. Seven fatalities occurred at this location.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A violent multiple-vortex tornado struck portions of extreme northern Georgia and southeast Tennessee during the mid-evening hours of April 27. It touched down along Davis Ridge Road in <a href="/wiki/Catoosa_County,_Georgia" title="Catoosa County, Georgia">Catoosa County, Georgia</a>, and moved through the town of <a href="/wiki/Ringgold,_Georgia" title="Ringgold, Georgia">Ringgold</a> at EF3 strength, destroying numerous homes and businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSRinggoldEF4_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSRinggoldEF4-132">[132]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Baymont_Inn_%26_Suites" title="Baymont Inn &amp; Suites">Baymont Inn &amp; Suites</a>, located near <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75" title="Interstate 75">Interstate 75</a> was partially destroyed by the tornado, along with a <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Taco_Bell" title="Taco Bell">Taco Bell</a>, and several gas stations located on Highway 151 in Ringgold at the Interstate 75 interchange (exit 348). The Catoosa County Department of Family and Children Services and other businesses on Nashville Street in downtown Ringgold were also heavily damaged. The Kellerhals Center for Visual Arts Education at Ringgold High School was destroyed (RHS itself had minor damage), and Ringgold Middle School was heavily damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSRinggoldEF4_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-NWSRinggoldEF4-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Past downtown Ringgold, the tornado reached EF4 intensity as it tore through a subdivision along Cherokee Valley Road at the north edge of town. Twelve homes were completely obliterated and swept away at that location (though they were not well-built). There were 74 destroyed homes and/or businesses, 60 with major damage, and 118 with minor damage for a total of 252 affected structures in the Ringgold area. Eight people were killed, mainly at the subdivision along Cherokee Valley Road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apison,_TN_tornado_damage.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="658" data-file-width="879" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Apison%2C_TN_tornado_damage.PNG/220px-Apison%2C_TN_tornado_damage.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Apison%2C_TN_tornado_damage.PNG/330px-Apison%2C_TN_tornado_damage.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Apison%2C_TN_tornado_damage.PNG/440px-Apison%2C_TN_tornado_damage.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apison,_TN_tornado_damage.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
High-end EF4 damage to a large brick home in Apison, TN.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The storm then crossed the Tennessee state line at 8:28 p.m. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EDT</a> (0028 UTC), and moved into <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_County,_Tennessee" title="Hamilton County, Tennessee">Hamilton County, Tennessee</a>, striking the small town of <a href="/wiki/Apison,_Tennessee" title="Apison, Tennessee">Apison</a> at high-end EF4 strength, where multiple large homes were leveled or swept away, 150 others were damaged, and thousands of trees were snapped and uprooted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSApisonEF4_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSApisonEF4-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The tornado then crossed into Bradley County at low-end EF4 strength, moving across the southern and eastern fringes of <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Tennessee" title="Cleveland, Tennessee">Cleveland</a> and affecting mainly residential areas, though a few businesses were damaged or destroyed as well. Subdivisions in the southern part of the city sustained major damage, with numerous houses destroyed and a few that were leveled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSApisonEF4_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-NWSApisonEF4-135">[135]</a></sup> Four people were killed in Cleveland, and many others were injured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSApisonEF4_135-2"><a href="#cite_note-NWSApisonEF4-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Several trees were felled in Polk County (as the tornado had weakened to EF1-strength), before the tornado crossed into McMinn County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSApisonEF4_135-3"><a href="#cite_note-NWSApisonEF4-135">[135]</a></sup> The tornado re-strengthened to an EF2 and destroyed two houses and a mobile home before lifting south of <a href="/wiki/Athens,_Tennessee" title="Athens, Tennessee">Athens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tornado killed 20 people and injured hundreds more along its 57-mile (92 km) path across Catoosa, Hamilton, Bradley, Polk and McMinn counties. The tornado was given a rating of EF4 with winds ranging from 175–190 mph (282–306 km/h). The damage path of the tornado was between <span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> and <span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> mile (0.54 and 0.80 km) wide. This tornado is only the eighth in Georgia to be categorized as an F4/EF4 on the (<a href="/wiki/Enhanced_Fujita_scale" title="Enhanced Fujita scale">Enhanced</a>) <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">Fujita scale</a>, since official tornado records have been kept in 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSRinggoldEF4_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-NWSRinggoldEF4-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSApisonEF4_135-4"><a href="#cite_note-NWSApisonEF4-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EF4_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-EF4-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>All roads in and out of Ringgold were closed until the morning of April 29; after roads leading to the affected areas were re-opened, residents and business owners were allowed to return, being allowed entry only by providing identification, and informing police a reason why they were entering into the area, in order to curb looting in the storm-damaged areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ringgold_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ringgold-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-tornadic_effects">Non-tornadic effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Non-tornadic effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/2011_Mississippi_River_floods" title="2011 Mississippi River floods">2011 Mississippi River floods</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="847" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg/220px-Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg/330px-Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg/440px-Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pcpnweekending04292011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rainfall totals within the United States for the week ending during the morning of April 29, 2011, which shows the extent of the heavy rain event this cyclone contributed towards.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This storm system prolonged an ongoing heavy rain event, which began across Arkansas and Missouri on April 22.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SS11_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-SS11-17">[17]</a></sup> Weekly rainfall totals reached 19.73 inches (501 mm) 6 miles (9.7 km) east-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Springdale,_Arkansas" title="Springdale, Arkansas">Springdale, Arkansas</a>, 16.20 inches (411 mm) 4 miles (6.4 km) northwest of <a href="/wiki/Poplar_Bluff,_Missouri" title="Poplar Bluff, Missouri">Poplar Bluff, Missouri</a>, and 14.96 inches (380 mm) at <a href="/wiki/Westville,_Oklahoma" title="Westville, Oklahoma">Westville, Oklahoma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> On April 25, 2011, thunderstorms with high winds swept through parts of southern and southeastern Ohio. Straight-line winds estimated at 80 miles per hour (130 km/h) uprooted trees, damaged roofs, and downed power lines through <a href="/wiki/Perry_County,_Ohio" title="Perry County, Ohio">Perry County, Ohio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Athens_County,_Ohio" title="Athens County, Ohio">Athens County, Ohio</a>. Strong thunderstorms and heavy downpours which led to flooding were also reported in multiple areas across Upstate New York with heavy flooding in the <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_New_York" title="Syracuse, New York">Syracuse</a> area. The rain also saturated hundreds of lakes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adirondack_mountains" title="Adirondack mountains">Adirondack mountains</a>. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_81" title="Interstate 81">Interstate 81</a> was briefly shut down in the downtown area at traffic hour and the <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_Upstate_Medical_University" title="State University of New York Upstate Medical University">State University of New York Upstate Medical University</a> also closed briefly due to flooding in the lobby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Farther south, flash flooding late on April 26 resulted in two fatalities in <a href="/wiki/Monroe,_Louisiana" title="Monroe, Louisiana">Monroe, Louisiana</a> after an apartment complex was swamped. The flooding there was considered to be worse than the flooding after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gustav" title="Hurricane Gustav">Hurricane Gustav</a> in <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In central and northern Arkansas, up to 10.44 inches (265 mm) of rain was reported during that week. The resulting flash flooding in central Arkansas also resulted in five people losing their lives. Many roads were closed due to the flooding there. The flooding was mitigated somewhat by a significant <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a> that had existed before the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Severe thunderstorms were reported as far north as <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ontario" title="Northern Ontario">Northern Ontario</a> on the evening of April 26. Heavy rains and minor flooding were also reported in Northern Ontario from April 26–28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Windstorms were also reported in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ontario" title="Southern Ontario">Southern Ontario</a> and Southern <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> which resulted in several injuries and one death, damages and power outages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ottawacitizen.com_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-ottawacitizen.com-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theweathernetwork.com_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-theweathernetwork.com-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fierce_winds_whip_through_Ontario_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fierce_winds_whip_through_Ontario-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMontreal_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMontreal-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zone-911_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zone-911-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
