<p>Other fatalities due to straight-line winds occurred in <a href="/wiki/McComb,_Mississippi" title="McComb, Mississippi">McComb, Mississippi</a> early on April 26<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apr25SPC_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Apr25SPC-22">[22]</a></sup> and also in <a href="/wiki/Moody,_Alabama" title="Moody, Alabama">Moody, Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vestavia_Hills,_Alabama" title="Vestavia Hills, Alabama">Vestavia Hills, Alabama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Franklin,_Tennessee" title="Franklin, Tennessee">Franklin, Tennessee</a> early on April 27 from the squall line with embedded tornadoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Reports_April_27_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Reports_April_27-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Reports_April_26_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Storm_Reports_April_26-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Alabama Governor <a href="/wiki/Robert_J._Bentley" title="Robert J. Bentley">Robert J. Bentley</a> declared a state of emergency in the state of Alabama on April 27, due to storm damage from severe thunderstorms earlier that day as well as forthcoming severe weather later that day. States of emergency were also declared in Arkansas, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, Mississippi, Missouri, <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, and Oklahoma because of the flooding and tornadoes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Following the tornado outbreak on the evening of April 27, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> granted a federal emergency declaration for the state of Alabama, giving federal assistance, including search and rescue assets, to the affected region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>More than 2,000 <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a> troops were deployed to Alabama, assisting local and state first responders in search and rescue efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> President Obama visited the affected areas of Alabama on April 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Also on April 29, he approved a federal disaster declaration for seven Mississippi counties: <a href="/wiki/Clarke_County,_Mississippi" title="Clarke County, Mississippi">Clarke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greene_County,_Mississippi" title="Greene County, Mississippi">Greene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinds_County,_Mississippi" title="Hinds County, Mississippi">Hinds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jasper_County,_Mississippi" title="Jasper County, Mississippi">Jasper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kemper_County,_Mississippi" title="Kemper County, Mississippi">Kemper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lafayette_County,_Mississippi" title="Lafayette County, Mississippi">Lafayette</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_Mississippi" title="Monroe County, Mississippi">Monroe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> By the morning of April 30, the Alabama Emergency Management Agency had confirmed at least 45 storm fatalities in Tuscaloosa, but this was later corrected downward to 44. The tornado killed 64 people along its entire path.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alemapressrelease1_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-alemapressrelease1-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity_outage">Electricity outage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Electricity outage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Storms through the area severely damaged <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Valley_Authority" title="Tennessee Valley Authority">Tennessee Valley Authority</a> (TVA)'s <a href="/wiki/Electric_power_transmission" title="Electric power transmission">power grid</a> for transmitting electricity throughout the region. More than 300 power transmission towers, 120 feet (37 m) to 150 feet (46 m) tall, were destroyed in the storms, some "twisted like bow ties" according to National Weather Service meteorologist Eric Holweg. The towers supported some 90 transmission lines, a mixture of 500<a href="/wiki/Volt" title="Volt">kV</a> and 161kV lines. Those lines provided power from TVA to 128 regional distributors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bowTieTower_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-bowTieTower-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electric_line_tower.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Electric_line_tower.jpg/220px-Electric_line_tower.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Electric_line_tower.jpg/330px-Electric_line_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Electric_line_tower.jpg/440px-Electric_line_tower.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electric_line_tower.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Transmission tower bent near <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville, Alabama</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>TVA lost the ability to transmit power from both <a href="/wiki/Browns_Ferry_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Browns Ferry Nuclear Power Plant">Browns Ferry Nuclear Power Plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Widows_Creek_Power_Plant" title="Widows Creek Power Plant">Widows Creek Fossil Plant</a> after the storms on April 27, requiring both to be shut down. The nuclear plant's <a href="/wiki/Shutdown_(nuclear_reactor)" title="Shutdown (nuclear reactor)">cold shutdown</a> was supported by diesel generators for four days until a second 161kV line could be restored to the plant. The loss of redundant off-site power required a "notification of unusual event", the lowest of four levels of concern dictated by the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Regulatory_Commission" title="Nuclear Regulatory Commission">NRC</a>. Some 60 percent of the sirens for warning residents of worse problems around Browns Ferry were disabled by the storms, and the plant had to arrange plans to use cars with loudspeakers to warn residents in case of another problem. Chief Operating Officer Bill McCollum of TVA stated that it could be weeks before the nuclear plant is up and running again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TFP-nuke_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-TFP-nuke-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bowTieTower_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-bowTieTower-160">[160]</a></sup> The Nuclear Regulatory Commission stated at a press conference: "The plants' conditions are stable and are being placed in a cooled-down condition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UPI-nuke_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-UPI-nuke-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville</a> was the largest city with no electricity from TVA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bowTieTower_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-bowTieTower-160">[160]</a></sup> All the traffic lights were off, a dusk-to-dawn curfew was imposed, students were sent home from <a href="/wiki/United_States_Space_Camp" title="United States Space Camp">United States Space Camp</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Panoply_Arts_Festival" title="Panoply Arts Festival">Panoply Arts Festival</a> was canceled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> Power was restored gradually to Huntsville, beginning with 3 percent on the morning of May 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3percent_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-3percent-166">[166]</a></sup> Only localized outages remained eight days after the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> In addition to traffic and safety issues, the outage caused difficulties with water treatment and distribution and retail of all kinds, including <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> and food purchases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3percent_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-3percent-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ontario electricity outages were minor, mostly caused by the windstorms of April 28. Although they affected thousands of people at different times throughout the day, all power was restored by the end of the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ottawacitizen.com_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-ottawacitizen.com-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theweathernetwork.com_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-theweathernetwork.com-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fierce_winds_whip_through_Ontario_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fierce_winds_whip_through_Ontario-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMontreal_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-JMontreal-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zone-911_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zone-911-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Super_Outbreak&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_tornadoes_and_tornado_outbreaks" title="List of North American tornadoes and tornado outbreaks">List of North American tornadoes and tornado outbreaks</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_F5_and_EF5_tornadoes" title="List of F5 and EF5 tornadoes">List of F5 and EF5 tornadoes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tornadoes_of_2011" title="Tornadoes of 2011">Tornadoes of 2011</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_disasters_in_the_United_States_by_death_toll" title="List of disasters in the United States by death toll">List of disasters in the United States by death toll</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tornado_records" title="Tornado records">Tornado records</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tri-State_Tornado" title="Tri-State Tornado">Tri-State Tornado</a> – Deadliest tornado in North America, and made March 18, 1925 the deadliest tornado day recorded in United States.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1932_Deep_South_tornado_outbreak" title="1932 Deep South tornado outbreak">1932 Deep South tornado outbreak</a> – Deadliest tornado outbreak in Alabama history, including an F4 tornado that tracked through Tuscaloosa.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1936_Tupelo%E2%80%93Gainesville_tornado_outbreak" title="1936 Tupelo–Gainesville tornado outbreak">1936 Tupelo–Gainesville tornado outbreak</a> – Infamous tornado outbreak occurring on April 5–6, 1936. Deadliest U.S. tornado outbreak since the March 1925 (Tri-State Tornado) outbreak, thus surpassing the March 1932, April 1974, and April 2011 outbreaks in total fatalities.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_1956_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1956 Birmingham tornado">April 1956 Birmingham tornado</a> – F4 tornado that hit the northern Birmingham suburbs on April 15, 1956.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1974_Super_Outbreak" title="1974 Super Outbreak">1974 Super Outbreak</a> – Infamous tornado outbreak occurring on April 3–4, 1974, similar in severity to the 2011 Super Outbreak; though the 2011 event surpassed the 1974 Super Outbreak as the largest recorded outbreak.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/April_1977_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1977 Birmingham tornado">April 1977 Birmingham tornado</a> – F5 tornado that hit the northern Birmingham suburbs on April 4, 1977.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/1994_Palm_Sunday_tornado_outbreak" title="1994 Palm Sunday tornado outbreak">1994 Palm Sunday tornado outbreak</a> – March 27, 1994 outbreak that produced an F4 tornado in St. Clair, Calhoun and Cherokee Counties in north-central Alabama.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_1998_Birmingham_tornado" title="April 1998 Birmingham tornado">April 1998 Birmingham tornado</a> – F5 tornado that struck western parts of Birmingham on April 8, 1998.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/December_2000_Tuscaloosa_tornado" title="December 2000 Tuscaloosa tornado">December 2000 Tuscaloosa tornado</a> – F4 tornado that hit southeast suburbs of Tuscaloosa on December 16, 2000.</li>
</ul>
